=== Depositions ===

Initial depositions were taken before the Intelligence, Foreign Affairs, and Oversight [[List of United States House of Representatives committees|House committees]], meeting jointly in a secure room, a [[Sensitive Compartmented Information Facility]] (SCIF) in the basement of the [[United States Capitol|U.S. Capitol]].<ref name="behind closed doors">{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/10/23/us/politics/on-politics-impeachment-scif.html |title=Behind Closed Doors |last=Lerer |first=Lisa |date=October 23, 2019 |work=The New York Times|access-date=November 1, 2019 |language=en-US |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> Only members of the three committees (47 Republicans and 57 Democrats) were permitted to attend. Witnesses were questioned by staff lawyers, and committee members were allowed to ask questions, with equal time being given to Republicans and Democrats. Transcripts were expected to be released and public hearings to be held at some time in the future.<ref name="really">{{Cite news |url=https://www.latimes.com/politics/story/2019-10-23/impeachment-deposition-room-stormed-by-republicans |title=What's really happening inside the impeachment inquiry room stormed by Republicans |last1=Haberkorn |first1=Jennifer |last2=Wire |first2=Sarah D. |date=October 23, 2019 |work=Los Angeles Times |accessdate=October 25, 2019}}</ref> Transcripts began to be released in early November, and public hearings were scheduled to begin on November 13.<ref name="first scheduled">{{cite news|url=https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/trump-impeachment-inquiry/first-public-hearings-trump-impeachment-inquiry-begin-next-week-schiff-n1077371|title=First public hearings in Trump impeachment inquiry to begin next week|last1=Shabad|first1=Rebecca|last2=Clark|first2=Dartunorro|date=November 6, 2019|work=NBC News|accessdate=November 10, 2019}}</ref>

On the morning of the Cipollone letter on October 8, 2019, [[Gordon Sondland]] had been scheduled to testify before the House committees regarding his involvement in the withholding of aid from Ukraine. However, he was instructed not to attend at the last minute by the State Department upon Trump's command.<ref name="borger">{{Cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2019/oct/08/impeachment-donald-trump-gordon-sondland-testimony-house-democrats |title=Trump says he blocked ambassador's testimony and attacks 'kangaroo court' |last1=Borger |first1=Julian |date=October 8, 2019 |work=[[The Guardian]] |accessdate=October 11, 2019 |last2=Pengelly |first2=Martin}}</ref>

==== Early depositions: October 11–17, 2019 ====

[[File:Opening Statement of Marie L.Yovanovitch to the House of Representatives committees.pdf|thumb|upright|Ambassador [[Marie Yovanovitch]]'s opening statement to her testimony before three House committees, October 11, 2019]]

[[Marie Yovanovitch]], the former ambassador to Ukraine, testified on October 11, 2019, in defiance of the White House although she remains an employee of the U.S. State Department. Yovanovitch told House committees she was "incredulous" at having been dismissed in May.<ref name="Yovanovitch lack of trust">{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/10/11/us/politics/marie-yovanovitch-trump-impeachment.html |title=Ukraine Envoy Says She Was Told Trump Wanted Her Out Over Lack of Trust |last=LaFraniere |first=Sharon |date=October 11, 2019 |work=The New York Times|access-date=October 14, 2019 |last2=Fandos |first2=Nicholas |issn=0362-4331 |last3=Kramer |first3=Andrew E.}}</ref> She described the State Department as "attacked and hollowed out from within".<ref name="Yovanovitch lack of trust" /> Yovanovitch testified that she had never met or spoken with Hunter Biden and that Joe Biden had never raised the subject of his son or the Ukrainian gas firm that employed him.<ref name="ousted false claims">{{Cite news |work=BBC News |title=Trump impeachment: Marie Yovanovitch says she was ousted over 'false claims' |accessdate=October 11, 2019 |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-50018043 |date=October 12, 2019}}</ref> During his July 25 phone call with Zelensky, Trump called Yovanovitch "bad news" and mentioned that "[s]he's going to go through some things".<ref name="Guardian Yovanovitch">{{Cite news |website=The Guardian |title=Who is Marie Yovanovitch, the diplomat defying Trump to testify on Ukraine? |accessdate=October 11, 2019 |date=October 11, 2019 |first=Julian |last=Borger |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2019/oct/11/who-is-marie-yovanovitch-diplomat-slated-to-testify-on-ukraine-and-trump}}</ref><ref name="Time Yovanovitch">{{Cite news |work=[[Time (magazine)|Time]] |title='Careful, Meticulous, Whip Smart'. Here's What to Know About the Ukraine Ambassador Trump Recalled |accessdate=October 11, 2019 |url=https://time.com/5698930/marie-yovanovitch-former-us-envoy-ukraine/ |date=October 11, 2019 |first=Adam |last=Geller |first2=Jocelyn |last2=Noveck}}</ref>

A former adviser to the president on Russian affairs, [[Fiona Hill (presidential advisor)|Fiona Hill]], testified before congressional investigators on October 14, 2019.<ref name="NPR Fiona Hill">{{cite web |url=https://www.npr.org/2019/10/14/769927362/trumps-former-russia-adviser-set-to-testify-as-part-of-impeachment-inquiry |first=Bobby |last=Allyn |date=October 14, 2019 |title=Trump's Former Russia Adviser Set To Testify As Part of Impeachment Inquiry |website=NPR|access-date=October 14, 2019}}</ref> She told the House committees that Giuliani circumvented State Department officials and diplomats, and that she had confronted Ambassador Sondland, who was assisting Giuliani in his efforts to pressure Ukraine into beginning investigations that would personally benefit Trump. After a meeting in which Sondland announced that there were "[Ukrainian] investigations that were dropped [and] need to be started up again" and under instruction from [[John Bolton]] (the [[National Security Advisor (United States)|National Security Advisor]] from April 2018 to September 2019), Hill expressed her and Bolton's concerns about Giuliani's activities to [[John Eisenberg]], an attorney for the NSC.<ref name="Demirjian 2019-10-14">{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/national-security/trumps-former-top-russia-adviser-to-testify-in-house-impeachment-probe/2019/10/14/e6015c1c-ee34-11e9-8693-f487e46784aa_story.html |title=Trump's ex-Russia adviser told impeachment investigators of Giuliani's efforts in Ukraine |last=Demirjian |first=Karoun |date=October 14, 2019 |work=The Washington Post|access-date=October 15, 2019 |last2=Harris |first2=Shane |last3=Rachael |first3=Bade}}</ref><ref name="Giuliani hand grenade">{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/10/14/us/politics/bolton-giuliani-fiona-hill-testimony.html |title=Bolton Objected to Ukraine Pressure Campaign, Calling Giuliani 'a Hand Grenade' |last=Baker |first=Peter |date=October 14, 2019 |work=The New York Times|access-date=October 15, 2019 |last2=Fandos |first2=Nicholas |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> Hill testified that she, Bolton, Volker, Energy Secretary Rick Perry,<ref name="Demirjian 2019-10-14" /> and two Ukrainian officials,<ref name="Giuliani hand grenade" /> were at that meeting on July 10, 2019,<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/10/14/politics/who-is-fiona-hill/index.html |title=Trump's former top Russia adviser told Congress she saw 'wrongdoing' in U.S. policy toward Ukraine, source says |last=Raju |first=Manu |last2=Herb |first2=Jeremy |date=October 15, 2019 |website=CNN |access-date=October 15, 2019 |last3=Cole |first3=Devan |last4=Borger |first4=Gloria |last5=Acosta |first5=Jim}}</ref> and that Bolton was furious after the meeting when he told her he was "not part of whatever drug deal Sondland and Mulvaney are cooking up".<ref>{{cite web |url=https://apnews.com/cddf98a0a5944b64a87386b971213ece |title=Sondland prepared to deny he was warned about Ukraine work |last=Tucker |first=Eric |date=October 15, 2019 |website=AP News |access-date=October 15, 2019}}</ref><ref name="Giuliani hand grenade" /> Hill told the committees that Giuliani was running a rogue foreign policy while informing the president's official advisers but leaving them powerless to stop it.<ref name="Giuliani hand grenade" /> When she confronted Sondland, who she believed was involved in affairs outside his position's purview, he claimed that, according to Trump, he was in charge of Ukraine matters.<ref name="Giuliani hand grenade" />

[[George P. Kent|George Kent]], [[Deputy Assistant Secretary]] for [[Bureau of European and Eurasian Affairs|European and Eurasian Affairs]], appeared before the Intelligence, Foreign Affairs and Oversight House committees on October 15, 2019.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.cbsnews.com/live-news/trump-impeachment-inquiry-latest-george-kent-testimony-2019-10-15/ |title=Giuliani defies congressional subpoena in impeachment inquiry |last=Tillett |first=Emily |last2=Watson |first2=Kathryn |date=October 15, 2019 |website=CBS News |access-date=October 15, 2019 |last3=Segers |first3=Grace}}</ref> Kent is the second current State Department official to defy White House instructions and comply with House subpoenas to testify before the committees.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/10/15/us/politics/impeachment-george-kent-state.html |title=Impeachment Investigators Question George Kent, State Dept. Ukraine Expert |last=Fandos |first=Nicholas |date=October 15, 2019 |work=The New York Times|access-date=October 15, 2019 |last2=Vogel |first2=Kenneth P. |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> According to Representative [[Gerry Connolly]] (D-Virginia), Kent testified that, during a meeting at the White House on May 23 organized by Mulvaney,<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/congress/vivid-details-emerge-on-ukraine-as-impeachment-quickens/2019/10/15/94d063ce-efba-11e9-bb7e-d2026ee0c199_story.html |title=Vivid details emerge on Ukraine as impeachment quickens |last=Mascaro |first=Lisa |last2=Jalonick |first2=Mary Clare |date=October 15, 2019 |work=The Washington Post |access-date=October 16, 2019 |last3=Kellman |first3=Laurie |agency=Associated Press}}</ref> Sondland, Volker, and Perry, who called themselves the "three amigos",<ref name="Three amigos">{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/top-state-department-official-expected-to-face-questions-about-ukraine-and-giuliani/2019/10/14/8ba23d18-eeca-11e9-b2da-606ba1ef30e3_story.html |title=White House directed 'three amigos' to run Ukraine policy, senior State department official tells House investigators |last=Kane |first=Paul |last2=Demirjian |first2=Karoun |date=October 15, 2019 |work=The Washington Post |access-date=October 16, 2019 |last3=Bade |first3=Rachael}}</ref><ref name="replaced pro staff with three amigos">{{cite web |url=https://www.npr.org/2019/10/15/770482694/wh-replaced-pro-ukraine-staff-with-three-amigos-congress-reportedly-told |title=White House Reportedly Replaced Ukraine Policy Staff With 'Three Amigos' |last=Ewing |first=Philip |date=October 15, 2019 |website=NPR |access-date=October 16, 2019}}</ref> had declared that they were now responsible for Ukrainian affairs.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/10/15/us/politics/impeachment-george-kent-state.html |title=Senior State Dept. Ukraine Expert Says White House Sidelined Him |last=Fandos |first=Nicholas |date=October 15, 2019 |work=The New York Times|access-date=October 16, 2019 |last2=Vogel |first2=Kenneth P. |issn=0362-4331 |last3=Shear |first3=Michael D.}}</ref> Connolly also said Kent testified that he had been directed to "lay low" and to focus on foreign relations with the five other countries in his purview.<ref name="Three amigos" />
[[File:Gordon Sondland - Opening Statement before the House of Representatives Committees.pdf|thumb|upright|Ambassador [[Gordon Sondland]]'s opening statement to his testimony before three House committees, October 17, 2019]]

A former senior adviser to Secretary Pompeo, [[Michael McKinley]], testified on October 16, 2019, after having resigned from his position the previous week.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/10/16/politics/who-is-mike-mckinley/index.html |title=A senior adviser to Mike Pompeo just resigned. Now he's set to testify in the impeachment probe |last=Hansler |first=Jennifer |last2=Atwood |first2=Kylie |date=October 16, 2019 |website=CNN |access-date=October 16, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/trump-impeachment-inquiry-live-updates/2019/10/14/b1ae2a70-ee08-11e9-8693-f487e46784aa_story.html |title=McKinley to testify Wednesday; Democrats mull whether to question Bolton |last=Sonmez |first=Felicia |date=October 14, 2019 |work=The Washington Post|access-date=October 16, 2019 |last2=Wagner |first2=John |last3=Shammas |first3=Brittany}}</ref> McKinley testified that he had resigned from his position out of frustration with the Trump administration and the recall of Ambassador Yovanovitch was the "last straw".<ref name="NYT McKinley">{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/10/16/us/mckinley-impeachment-ukraine.html |title=Former Top State Dept. Aide Tells Impeachment Investigators He Quit Over Ukraine |last=Fandos |first=Nicholas |date=October 16, 2019 |work=The New York Times|access-date=October 17, 2019 |last2=Barnes |first2=Julian E. |issn=0362-4331 |last3=Shear |first3=Michael D.}}</ref> In his opening remarks, he said "[t]he timing of my resignation was the result of two overriding concerns: the failure, in my view, of the State Department to offer support to [[United States Foreign Service|Foreign Service]] employees caught up in the impeachment inquiry on Ukraine and, second, by what appears to be the utilization of our ambassadors overseas to advance a domestic political objective."<ref name="NYT McKinley" /><ref name="NPR McKinley">{{cite web |url=https://www.npr.org/2019/10/16/770643839/ex-pompeo-aide-is-latest-state-department-official-to-talk-in-impeachment-inquir |title=Ex-Pompeo Aide Is Latest State Department Official To Talk In Impeachment Inquiry |last=Booker |first=Brakkton |date=October 16, 2019 |website=NPR |access-date=October 17, 2019}}</ref> McKinley said he was "disturbed by the implication that foreign governments were being approached to procure negative information on political opponents".<ref name="NPR McKinley" />

Before appearing in front of three House committees on October 17, 2019, Ambassador Sondland publicly released his opening remarks.<ref name="Becket 2019-10-17" /> He testified that Trump had refused to meet with the Ukrainian president without preconditions and that, in a May 23 meeting, State Department officials were directed to work with Giuliani to address Trump's "concerns" about the Ukrainian government.<ref name="NYT Sondland Giuliani">{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/10/17/us/politics/gordon-sondland-testimony.html |title=Gordon Sondland, E.U. Envoy, Testifies Trump Delegated Ukraine Policy to Giuliani |last=Fandos |first=Nicholas |date=October 17, 2019 |work=The New York Times|access-date=October 19, 2019 |last2=Schmidt |first2=Michael S. |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> Sondland claimed he was ignorant of Giuliani's intentions and had no choice but to work with the president's personal attorney. According to ''The New York Times'', this conflicts with previous testimony given during the inquiry in which other State Department officials testified that Sondland was "a willing participant who inserted himself into Ukraine policy even though the country is not in the purview of his posting, and was a key player in [Trump]'s efforts to win a commitment from the new Ukrainian government to investigate his political rivals."<ref name="NYT Sondland Giuliani" /> ''[[The Washington Post]]'' also disputes this claim, asserting that it conflicts with the known timeline of events. According to ''The Washington Post'', "In the weeks leading up to that May 23 White House briefing, Giuliani's and even Trump's interest in spotlighting the Bidens' actions in Ukraine were hardly a secret."<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/10/17/this-central-claim-gordon-sondlands-testimony-just-doesnt-add-up/ |title=This central claim in Gordon Sondland's testimony just doesn't add up |last=Blake |first=Aaron |date=October 17, 2019 |work=The Washington Post |access-date=October 19, 2019}}</ref>

==== Bill Taylor ====

[[File:Opening statement of Ambassador William B. Taylor (searchable).pdf|thumb|upright|Ambassador [[William B. Taylor Jr.|Bill Taylor]]'s opening statement to his testimony before three House committees, October 22, 2019]]

On October 22, 2019, [[William B. Taylor Jr.|Bill Taylor]], the senior U.S. diplomatic official in Ukraine, testified to Congressional investigators. Taylor testified that he had learned in mid-July 2019 that a potential White House meeting between Trump and Zelensky "was conditioned on the investigations of Burisma and alleged Ukrainian interference in the 2016 U.S. elections", and that he later was told, in September 2019, that U.S. military aid to Ukraine was also dependent on such investigations—including into the Bidens.<ref name="bade">{{cite news |last1=Bade |first1=Rachael |last2=Gearan |first2=Anne |last3=Demirjan |first3=Karoun |last4=DeBonis |first4=Mike |title=Trump made Ukraine aid contingent on public pledge to investigate Bidens and 2016 election, U.S. envoy says he was told |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/powerpost/diplomat-who-raised-alarm-about-withholding-aid-to-ukraine-testifies-in-impeachment-probe/2019/10/22/086fb850-f436-11e9-8cf0-4cc99f74d127_story.html |date=October 22, 2019 |work=[[The Washington Post]] |accessdate=October 28, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Wu |first1=Nicholas |last2=Jansen |first2=Bart |title=Key takeaways from Ukraine diplomat Bill Taylor's 'explosive' opening statement |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2019/10/22/impeachment-takeaways-ukraine-diplomat-bill-taylors-testimony/2450332001/ |accessdate=October 24, 2019 |work=[[USA Today]] |date=October 22, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Faulders |first1=Katherine |title=Top U.S. diplomat in Ukraine tells Congress investigating Bidens and election interference tied to aid money |url=https://abcnews.go.com/Politics/top-us-diplomat-ukraine-tells-congress-investigating-bidens/story?id=66451155 |accessdate=October 24, 2019 |work=[[ABC News]] |date=October 22, 2019}}</ref>

Taylor testified that, alongside the "regular, formal diplomatic processes" with Ukraine led by himself, there was a "highly irregular", "informal channel of U.S. policy-making" concerning Ukraine. The informal channel began in May 2019, being "guided" by Giuliani, and also involving Volker, Sondland and Perry. Taylor said that by August 2019 he had realized the informal channel "was running contrary to the goals of longstanding U.S. policy", while the formal channel wanted "a strong U.S.–Ukraine partnership". According to Taylor, the informal channel had "driven" the idea of a White House meeting between the presidents being conditional on the investigations.<ref name=":3b" /><ref>{{Cite news |last1=Jaffe |first1=Greg |last2=Miller |first2=Greg |title='Alarming circumstances': A distressed diplomat tells a tale of venal intrigue |date=October 23, 2019 |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/national-security/alarming-circumstances-a-distressed-diplomat-tells-a-tale-of-venal-intrigue/2019/10/22/935b23c6-f500-11e9-ad8b-85e2aa00b5ce_story.html |accessdate=October 24, 2019 |work=The Washington Post}}</ref>

Taylor noted that, during a June 2019 call between himself, Zelensky, Sondland, Volker and Perry; Sondland had said "he did not wish to include most of the regular interagency participants" and that "he wanted to make sure no one was transcribing or monitoring." As for Trump's July 2019 call with Zelensky, Taylor said he did not receive any report regarding the call from the White House even though he was scheduled to meet Zelensky a day later.<ref name=":3b" />

Taylor said he heard from NSC aide [[Tim Morrison (arms control expert)|Tim Morrison]] that, on September 1, Sondland told Zelensky aide {{ill|Andrey Yermak|WD=Q65200615|vertical-align=sup}} that the military aid to Ukraine was dependent on Zelensky's pursuit of the Burisma investigation. Taylor cited Sondland's telling him in a call that Trump wanted Zelensky to publicly announce he would order the two investigations, thus placing Zelensky "in a public box". Taylor quoted Sondland as saying "everything" including military aid and a Trump–Zelensky meeting was contingent upon that announcement.<ref name=":3b">{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/10/22/us/politics/william-taylor-testimony.html |title=6 Key Revelations of Taylor's Opening Statement to Impeachment Investigators |last=LaFraniere |first=Sharon |author-link=Sharon LaFraniere |date=October 22, 2019 |work=The New York Times |access-date=October 23, 2019|url-access=limited}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |last1=Blake |first1=Aaron |title=5 takeaways from William Taylor's huge opening statement |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/10/22/takeaways-bill-taylors-crucial-opening-statement/ |accessdate=October 24, 2019 |work=The Washington Post |date=October 23, 2019}}</ref>

According to Taylor, he wrote a first-person cable to Secretary Pompeo on advice from Bolton: "I wrote and transmitted such a cable on August 29, describing the 'folly' I saw in withholding military aid to Ukraine at a time when hostilities were still active in the east and when Russia was watching closely to gauge the level of American support for the Ukrainian government. I told the secretary that I could not and would not defend such a policy." Taylor reported that Pompeo gave no reply to his cable.<ref name=":3b" />

==== Republican protest and legal challenges ====

On October 23, 2019, Laura Cooper, the [[Deputy Assistant Secretary of Defense]] for Russia, Ukraine, and Eurasia,<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.defense.gov/Our-Story/Biographies/Biography/Article/1568391/laura-k-cooper/ |title=Laura K. Cooper: Deputy Assistant Secretary of Defense for Russia, Ukraine, Eurasia |website=[[United States Department of Defense]] |access-date=October 24, 2019}}</ref> testified in closed session before three Congressional committees.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/live/2019/oct/23/trump-news-today-live-impeachment-inquiry-biden-2020-democrats-latest-updates |title=Trump impeachment inquiry: key testimony finally begins despite Republican sit-in—as it happened |first=Maanvi |last=Singh |first2=Joan E. |last2=Greve |date=October 24, 2019 |work=The Guardian |access-date=October 24, 2019 |issn=0261-3077}}</ref> Cooper's testimony, originally scheduled for that morning, was delayed by roughly five hours when a group of House Republicans led by [[Matt Gaetz]] (R-Florida) stormed the SCIF where impeachment inquiry committee meetings are being held,<ref>{{cite web |url=https://thehill.com/homenews/house/467168-gop-lawmaker-shares-audio-of-phone-call-he-made-from-highly-classified-scif |title=GOP lawmaker shares audio of phone call he made from highly classified SCIF room |last=Folley |first=Aris |date=October 23, 2019 |website=The Hill |language=en|access-date=October 24, 2019}}</ref> and refused to leave, at one point ordering pizza.<ref>{{cite web |first=John |last=Gage |url=https://www.washingtonexaminer.com/news/brave-freedom-fighters-having-pizza-republicans-storming-closed-hearing-order-dominos |title='Brave freedom fighters having pizza': Republicans storming closed hearing order Domino's |date=October 23, 2019 |website=Washington Examiner |language=en|access-date=October 24, 2019}}</ref> The group protested what they asserted were secret Democratic hearings closed to Republicans,<ref>{{Cite tweet |user=SteveScalise |number=1187045316316536834 |title=Democrats are trying to deny Republican Members of Congress access to Schiff's secret impeachment proceedings. What are they hiding?? Enough is enough! The American people deserve transparency! This Democrat scheme to impeach @realDonaldTrump behind closed doors cannot continue. pic.twitter.com/ernM1x73m9 |last=Scalise |first=Steve |date=October 23, 2019 |access-date=October 25, 2019}}</ref> although 48 Republicans who are members of the three committees jointly holding the hearings were entitled to attend the hearings and some had done so. Thirteen of those members participated in the protest.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/10/23/heres-why-matt-gaetz-sit-in-stunt-was-particularly-weird/ |title=Here's why the Matt Gaetz sit-in stunt was particularly weird |first=Philip |last=Bump |newspaper=[[The Washington Post]] |date=October 23, 2019 |accessdate=October 25, 2019}}</ref> Democrats responded with criticism over the interruption and accused the Republicans of violating the rules governing the SCIF, which prohibit cell phones in the area.<ref name="auto3">{{Cite news |date=October 24, 2019 |url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/10/23/politics/republicans-storm-impeachment-inquiry-deposition-laura-cooper/index.html |title=After Republicans storm hearing room, Defense official testifies in impeachment inquiry |first=Manu |last=Raju |first2=Jeremy |last2=Herb |website=CNN |access-date=October 24, 2019}}</ref> After the protest ended, Cooper completed her testimony which lasted approximately 3.5 hours.<ref>{{Cite news |date=October 24, 2019 |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2019/10/23/impeachment-defense-official-laura-cooper-summoned-ukraine-aid/4064408002/ |title=GOP protest temporarily halts House Democratic impeachment deposition of Defense official Laura Cooper |last=Wu |first=Nicholas |last2=Jansen |first2=Bart |website=USA Today |language=en|access-date=October 24, 2019}}</ref> She was expected to speak about how the process works for transferring military aid to Ukraine.<ref name="auto3" /> She is believed to have tried to get the aid released.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/10/23/laura-cooper-ukraine-military-aid-056015 |title=Pentagon official testifies about withheld military aid to Ukraine |last1=Cheney |first1=Kyle |last2=Desiderio |first2=Andrew |last3=Morgan |first3=Wesley |date=October 23, 2019 |work=Politico |accessdate=October 24, 2019}}</ref> The next day it was revealed that her attorney had received a letter from the Pentagon telling her not to testify, citing an administration-wide policy against cooperating with the probe.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.pbs.org/newshour/politics/pentagon-told-impeachment-inquiry-witness-not-to-testify |title=Pentagon told impeachment inquiry witness not to testify |last=Tucker |first=Eric |date=October 24, 2019 |agency=Associated Press |work=PBS |accessdate=October 24, 2019}}</ref>

The House Judiciary Committee asked to see secret [[grand jury]] information that had been used in compiling the Mueller Report. The DOJ refused to turn it over, arguing that secrecy of grand jury material must be preserved and that the impeachment inquiry was invalid. On October 25, 2019, Federal Judge [[Beryl A. Howell]] ruled that the inquiry is valid and that the DOJ must forward the information to the committee within the week.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cnbc.com/2019/10/25/judge-orders-release-of-mueller-material-citing-impeachment-chance.html |title=Judge calls Trump impeachment probe legal, says House must get Mueller grand jury information |last=Mangan |first=Dan |date=October 25, 2019 |work=CNBC |accessdate=October 25, 2019}}</ref> DOJ attorneys had previously asserted that congressional investigators had "not yet exhausted [their] available [[Discovery (law)|discovery]] tools", arguments Howell said "smack of farce", as the administration had openly said it would [[Stonewalling|stonewall]] the investigation. Some legal analysts noted that a White House counsel letter to Democratic leaders days earlier stating the administration would not cooperate with the impeachment inquiry—which was widely derided as more of a political rather than a legal argument—<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.mediaite.com/trump/white-house-blasted-over-letter-refusing-to-cooperate-with-impeachment-inquiry-deranged-garbage/ |title=WH Blasted on Refusing to Cooperate With Impeachment Inquiry |last=Feldman |first=Josh |date=October 8, 2019 |website=[[Mediaite]] |publisher=[[Abrams Media]] |access-date=October 21, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/10/09/us/politics/trump-case-against-impeachment.html |title=Trump's Sweeping Case Against Impeachment Is a Political Strategy |last=Baker |first=Peter |date=October 9, 2019|url-access=limited |access-date=October 21, 2019 |newspaper=The New York Times}}</ref> may have backfired by contributing to Howell's rationale for her decision.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://lawandcrime.com/high-profile/federal-judge-calls-trump-admins-legal-arguments-a-farce-in-order-filled-with-jabs-at-doj-attorneys/ |title=Federal Judge Calls Trump Admin's Legal Arguments a 'Farce' in Order Filled with Jabs at DOJ Attorneys |last=Kalmbacher |first=Colin |date=October 25, 2019 |website=Law & Crime |access-date=October 25, 2019}}</ref>

[[Charles Kupperman]], Trump's deputy national security advisor from January to September 2019, filed a lawsuit on October 25, 2019, in which he asked a federal judge to rule which conflicting order he should follow: a subpoena from the House or an order from the White House not to appear. His attorney said that as a private citizen Kupperman is not able to choose which directive to obey, adding that "Constitutional disputes between the Legislative and Executive Branches should be adjudicated by the Judicial Branch".<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/politics-news/trump-national-security-official-asks-judge-whether-he-has-testify-n1072406 |title=Trump national security official asks judge whether he has to testify in impeachment probe |last1=Bennett |first1=Geoff |date=October 25, 2019 |work=NBC News |accessdate=October 27, 2019 |last2=Helsel |first2=Phil}}</ref><ref name="kupperman1" /> Hearings on the case were scheduled for December 2019.<ref name="impeachment before subpoena">{{cite web |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/10/31/house-impeachment-aide-subpoena-063453 |title=House could act on impeachment before suit over former Trump aide's subpoena is resolved |last=Gerstein |first=Josh |date=October 31, 2019 |website=Politico |language=en-US |access-date=November 1, 2019}}</ref> The subpoena was withdrawn on November 6, but the judge indicated the case will go on.<ref name = continue />

==== Alexander Vindman ====

[[File:Opening Statement of Lieutenant Colonel Alexander S. Vindman.pdf|thumb|upright|[[Alexander Vindman]]'s opening statement to his testimony before three House committees, October 29, 2019]]

On October 29, 2019, the NSC's head of European Affairs, Lieutenant Colonel [[Alexander Vindman]], testified before the House committees, stating he had overheard Trump's phone conversation with the Ukrainian President.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.armytimes.com/news/your-army/2019/10/29/purple-heart-ranger-tab-fao-meet-the-army-officer-testifying-about-trumps-ukraine-call/ |title=Purple Heart, Ranger tab, FAO: Meet the Army officer testifying about Trump's Ukraine call |first=Kyle |last=Rempfer |date=October 29, 2019 |website=Army Times}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/trump-impeachment-inquiry/extremely-disturbing-top-dems-alarmed-over-vindman-s-testimony-trump-n1073371 |title='Extremely disturbing': Top Democrats alarmed over Vindman's testimony on Trump–Ukraine call |website=NBC News |date=October 29, 2019 |first=Adam |last=Edelman |first2=Rebecca |last2=Shabad |accessdate=November 5, 2019}}</ref> He had released his opening statement the day before.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2019/10/29/us/politics/vindman-statement-impeachment.html |title=Read Alexander Vindman's Opening Statement on Trump and Ukraine |date=October 29, 2019 |website=The New York Times |access-date=October 29, 2019}}</ref> Vindman testified: "In Spring of 2019, I became aware of outside influencers promoting a false and alternative narrative of Ukraine inconsistent with the consensus views of the interagency, [which was] harmful to U.S. national security [and also] undermined U.S. government efforts to expand cooperation with Ukraine."<ref name="npr vindman">{{Cite news |first=Amita |last=Kelly |url=https://www.npr.org/2019/10/28/774256868/read-ukraine-expert-lt-col-alexander-vindmans-opening-statement |title=Read: Ukraine Expert Lt. Col. Alexander Vindman's Opening Statement |website=NPR |date=October 28, 2019 |access-date=October 29, 2019}}</ref>

Vindman said that, additionally, he was concerned by two events, both of which he objected to senior officials in real-time, and which he reported to the NSC's lead attorney. The first event occurred at a July 10 meeting between Ukraine's then [[National Security and Defense Council of Ukraine|Secretary of National Security and Defense Council]] [[Oleksandr Danylyuk|Oleksandr Danlylyuk]], and then U.S. National Security Advisor Bolton, at which Ambassadors Volker and Sondland, and Secretary Perry were in attendance. At the meeting, Sondland asked Ukraine to launch investigations into the Bidens to get a meeting with President Trump. Vindman states that Bolton cut the meeting short, and that both he and Fiona Hill told Ambassador Sondland his comments were inappropriate, and that he reported the concerns to the NSC's lead counsel.<ref>{{cite web |date=October 29, 2019 |url=https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/trump-impeachment-inquiry/read-national-security-official-alexander-s-vindman-s-prepared-remarks-n1073156 |title=Read national security official Alexander S. Vindman's prepared remarks to Congress |website=NBC News |language=en|access-date=October 29, 2019}}</ref>

The second event occurred on a July 25 phone call between President Trump and Zelensky. Vindman states, "I was concerned by the call. I did not think it was proper to demand that a foreign government investigate a U.S. citizen, and I was worried about the implications for the U.S. government's support of Ukraine. I realized that if Ukraine pursued an investigation into the Bidens and Burisma, it would likely be interpreted as a partisan play which would undoubtedly result in Ukraine losing the bipartisan support it has thus far maintained. This would all undermine U.S. national security." Vindman also reported this event to Eisenberg, the NSC's lead counsel.<ref name="npr vindman" /> Vindman also testified that the "rough transcript" of the call released by the White House omitted crucial words and phrases, including Trump asserting recordings of Joe Biden discussing Ukraine corruption exist, which Trump stated in the third set of [[ellipsis|ellipses]] in the released transcript. Vindman said he had tried but failed to restore the full transcript.<ref name="corrected"/> A senior White House official had asserted when the transcript was released that the ellipses "do not indicate missing words or phrases", but rather "a trailing off of a voice or pause".<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/politics/live-news/trump-impeachment-inquiry-09-25-2019/h_08149725b4b299fa4849b4fd8afb3ecb |title=Here's why there are ellipses in the White House transcript |date=September 25, 2019 |website=[[CNN]] |first=Pamela |last=Brown}}</ref> Trump had previously characterized the released transcript as "an exact word-for-word transcript of the conversation".<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2019/10/03/odd-markings-ellipses-fuel-doubts-about-rough-transcript-trumps-ukraine-call/ |date=October 2, 2019 |title=Odd markings, ellipses fuel doubts about the rough transcript of Trump's Ukraine call |first1=Carol D. |last1=Leonnig |first2=Craig |last2=Timberg |first3=Drew |last3=Harwell |website=Washington Post}}</ref>

Vindman also testified that the "rough transcript" of the July 25 phone call omitted President Zelensky stating the name Burisma (the natural gas company on whose board Hunter Biden sat), and substituted it with the phrase "the company that you mentioned in this issue".<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/white-house-official-who-heard-trumps-call-with-ukraine-leader-testified-that-he-was-told-to-keep-quiet/2019/11/01/dbed7fae-fc07-11e9-ac8c-8eced29ca6ef_story.html |title=White House official who heard Trump's call with Ukraine leader testified that he was told to keep quiet |last=Hamburger |first=Tom |date=November 1, 2019 |work=The Washington Post|access-date=November 2, 2019 |last2=Leonnig |first2=Carol D. |last3=Miller |first3=Greg |last4=Nakashima |first4=Ellen}}</ref>

==== October 30–31, 2019 ====

On October 30, 2019, [[Catherine Croft]], a State Department Ukraine expert and NSC staff member testified. She noted in her opening statement that she was aware of Giuliani's communication with Volker, though she was not involved with those discussions, that former Republican lawmaker [[Bob Livingston]] repeatedly called her to promote the removal of Ambassador [[Marie Yovanovitch|Yovanovitch]]. She added: "On July 18, I participated in a sub-Policy Coordination Committee video conference where an [<nowiki/>[[Office of Management and Budget]] (OMB)] representative reported that the White House Chief of Staff, Mick Mulvaney, had placed an informal hold on security assistance to Ukraine. The only reason given was that the order came in the direction of the President."<ref name="NPR 2019-10-30" /><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/more-impeachment-witnesses-to-go-before-lawmakers-11572211062 |title=More Impeachment Witnesses to Go Before Lawmakers |last=Ballhaus |first=Rebecca |last2=Salama |first2=Vivian |date=October 27, 2019 |website=The Wall Street Journal |language=en-US |access-date=October 31, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/house-panels-hear-officialsconcerns-about-trumps-ukraine-call-11572357591 |title=Parties Spar Over White House Aide in Combative Impeachment Hearing |last=Volz |first=Dustin |last2=Restuccia |first2=Andrew |date=October 29, 2019 |website=The Wall Street Journal |language=en-US |access-date=October 31, 2019 |last3=Hughes |first3=Siobhan}}</ref>

[[Christopher J. Anderson]], a career Foreign Service officer who succeeded Croft as an adviser to Volker, was also deposed the same day.<ref name="trump dark view of ukraine">{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/national-security/testimony-from-career-diplomats-to-outline-trumps-dark-view-of-ukraine/2019/10/29/1681d293-f23c-476a-bdd8-35244e23d66a_story.html |title=Testimony from career diplomats outlines Trump's dark view of Ukraine |last=Hudson |first=John |last2=Viebeck |first2=Elise |date=October 30, 2019 |work=The Washington Post |access-date=October 31, 2019}}</ref><ref name="Bolton subpoenaed">{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/10/30/us/politics/robert-livingston-ukraine-impeachment.html |title=John Bolton Is Summoned to Testify in Trump Impeachment Inquiry |last=Fandos |first=Nicholas |date=October 30, 2019 |work=The New York Times|access-date=October 31, 2019 |last2=Goldman |first2=Adam |language=en-US |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> In his opening statement, Anderson said he and Volker had attempted to satisfy Giuliani while at same time assisting the Ukrainian government to fight corruption and build a relationship with the U.S. However, their efforts repeatedly conflicted with Giuliani's.<ref name="Bolton subpoenaed" /> Anderson confirmed that Bolton had concerns with Giuliani's involvement in Ukraine affairs, and that he had written a memo summarizing Bolton's concerns to share with other State Department officials including Kent.<ref name="Bolton subpoenaed" /> Anderson also noted that he and several other State Department officials prepared a statement condemning the [[Russian military intervention in Ukraine]] after the [[Kerch Strait incident|2018 attack on Ukrainian vessels]] in the [[Sea of Azov]]. However, the statement was blocked from publication by the White House.<ref name="trump dark view of ukraine" />

Tim Morrison, an official on the NSC, testified in a closed-door session on October 31. Morrison corroborated previous testimony by [[William B. Taylor Jr.|Bill Taylor]], saying Taylor had been "accurate" on the "substance" of their conversations, but there were two differences in the details, the first being a location of a meeting. Regarding the second difference, Morrison testified that in his September{{nbsp}}1 conversation with Sondland, he learned that Sondland had proposed to Ukrainian presidential advisor Andriy Yermak that military aid to Ukraine was "conditioned on a public statement" by the new Ukrainian prosecutor general's reopening an investigation into Burisma. (Taylor's testimony was that Zelensky should make the announcement.)<ref name=Leonnig-191031 /><ref>{{cite news |last1=Fandos |first1=Nicholas |title=White House Aide Confirms He Saw Signs of a Quid Pro Quo on Ukraine |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/10/31/us/politics/morrison-testimony-impeachment.html |accessdate=November 3, 2019 |work=[[The New York Times]] |date=October 31, 2019 |archive-url=https://archive.today/20191031192539/https://www.nytimes.com/2019/10/31/us/politics/morrison-testimony-impeachment.html |archive-date=October 31, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=House |first1=Billy |title=White House Aide Tells House of Concerns Over Trump and Ukraine |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/amp/news/articles/2019-11-01/white-house-aide-tells-house-of-concerns-over-trump-and-ukraine |accessdate=November 3, 2019 |work=[[Bloomberg News]] |date=October 31, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Treene |first1=Alayna |last2=Ayesh |first2=Rashaan |title=Former White House official confirms top Ukraine diplomat's testimony |url=https://www.axios.com/white-house-tim-morrison-diplomat-testimony-c77aa24b-ccf6-46f0-bad5-199d45e434e7.html |accessdate=November 3, 2019 |work=[[Axios (website)|Axios]] |date=November 1, 2019}}</ref> Morrison also discussed the July 2019 Trump–Zelensky call, having listened to the call himself. He told lawmakers he "promptly" brought concerns about the call to White House lawyers because he worried a summary would be leaked with negative consequences, but he said he did not necessarily think anything illegal was discussed.<ref name=Leonnig-191031>{{cite news | url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/national-security-council-official-set-to-testify-in-impeachment-inquiry-is-leaving-his-post/2019/10/30/261285c6-fb62-11e9-8190-6be4deb56e01_story.html | title=White House official corroborates diplomat's account that Trump appeared to seek quid pro quo | work=[[The Washington Post]] | date=October 31, 2019 | accessdate=October 31, 2019 | first=Carol | last=Leonnig | first2=John | last2=Hudson | first3=Karoun | last3=Demirjian}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|website=CBS News|date=Oct 31, 2019|url=https://www.cbsnews.com/live-news/trump-impeachment-house-resolution-vote-latest-today-2019-10-31-live-updates/|title=White House official wasn't concerned "anything illegal" occurred on Trump's Ukraine call|last1=Segers|first1=Grace|last2=Watson|first2=Kathryn|last3=Stefan|first3=Becket}}</ref>

==== White House officials refuse to be deposed ====

Democrats had hoped to hear from four current White House officials on November 4, including John Eisenberg, deputy counsel to the president for National Security Affairs; [[Michael Ellis (Trump administration official)|Michael Ellis]], senior associate counsel to the president; [[Robert Blair (U.S. president aide)|Robert Blair]], a top aide to the chief of staff; and Brian McCormack, an official with the Office of Management and Budget (OMB). Like former deputy national security adviser Charles Kupperman, Blair is waiting for the courts to solve a conflict between the White House prohibition and a congressional subpoena. The case is scheduled to be decided in December;<ref name="ABC">{{Cite news |url=https://abcnews.go.com/Politics/white-house-officials-slated-depositions-impeachment-inquiry-expected/story?id=66730843 |title=4 White House officials slated for depositions in impeachment inquiry not expected to show up |last=Faulders |first=Katherine |date=November 4, 2019 |work=ABC News|access-date=November 4, 2019 |last2=Santucci |first2=John |last3=Siegel |first3=Benjamin}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |website=The New Civil Rights Movement |date=November 4, 2019 |title=White House Blocks Four Administration Witnesses From Giving Impeachment Depositions |first=Travis |last=Gettys |url=https://www.thenewcivilrightsmovement.com/2019/11/white-house-blocks-four-administration-witnesses-from-giving-impeachment-depositions/}}</ref>{{needs update|date=December 2019}} the same month, Blair was promoted.<ref>{{cite web |last=Rozsa |first=Matthew |title=Key Trump aide gets big promotion after refusing to testify in impeachment probe |url=https://www.salon.com/2019/12/24/key-trump-aide-gets-big-promotion-after-refusing-to-testify-in-impeachment-probe/ |website=Salon |accessdate=December 25, 2019 |date=December 24, 2019}}</ref>

Michael Duffey, OMB's associate director for National Security Programs, and acting OMB Director [[Russell Vought]], did not appear for scheduled closed-door depositions on November{{nbsp}}5 and 6, respectively. Ulrich Brechbuhl, Counselor of the State Department, defied the subpoena for November{{nbsp}}6 and traveled to Europe with Pompeo instead.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/06/politics/pompeo-state-impeachment-confidence/index.html |title=Pompeo has lost confidence at State amid impeachment probe |last=Warren |first=Michael |last2=Atwood |first2=Kylie |date=November 6, 2019 |website=CNN |access-date=November 7, 2019}}</ref> Bolton said he would not voluntarily testify on November 7, and was expected to legally challenge a subpoena,<ref name=ABC /> and threatened to sue if committees issued a subpoena.<ref>{{Cite news |first=Patricia |last=Zengerle |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-trump-impeachment-bolton-idUSKBN1XH2BU|title=Former Trump adviser Bolton threatened to sue if subpoenaed to testify in impeachment probe: committee|date=November 7, 2019|work=Reuters|access-date=December 17, 2019|language=en}}</ref> House investigators subsequently withdrew the subpoena.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/11/06/house-withdraws-bolton-aide-subpoena-066941 |date=November 6, 2019 |title=House withdraws subpoena for top Bolton aide|last=Cheney|first=Kyle|website=[[Politico]]|language=en|access-date=December 17, 2019}}</ref>

==== November 6–8, 2019 ====

On November 6, 2019, David Hale, the undersecretary of State for political affairs, testified for several hours on the subject of the ouster of Yovanovitch.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rollcall.com/news/congress/impeachment-news-roundup-nov-6|title=Impeachment news roundup: Nov. 6|date=November 6, 2019|work=Roll Call|access-date=November 7, 2019|language=en-US}}</ref> Jennifer Williams, a special advisor to United States Vice President Mike Pence on European and Russian affairs, who happened to be listening in on the July 25 call, testified on November 7, 2019.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/07/politics/mike-pence-ukraine-house-democrats-impeachment/index.html|title=House to explore Pence's role in Ukraine controversy with new testimony|last=Klein|first=Betsy|last2=Collins|first2=Kaitlan|date=November 7, 2019|website=CNN|access-date=November 7, 2019|last3=Marsh|first3=Rene}}</ref>

==== November 15–16, 2019 ====

[[File:David-Holmes-Opening-Statement.pdf|thumb|upright|David Holmes's opening statement to his deposition on November 15, 2019]]

On November 15, David Holmes, a U.S. Department of State foreign service officer who works at the U.S. embassy in Ukraine, and serves as an aide to Bill Taylor, testified in a closed-door session before three House committees that he and two unnamed aides overheard a phone conversation between Ambassador Sondland and President Trump, while at a restaurant in [[Kyiv]], and immediately following a private meeting between President Zelensky and Sondland, where Trump asked Sondland about whether or not the Ukrainian President had agreed to investigate the Bidens.<ref name=holmesdeposition>{{cite news |first=Alayna |date=November 14, 2019 |last=Treene |url=https://www.axios.com/donald-trump-impeachment-david-holmes-mark-sandy-67051991-a73a-4bd1-aa45-e02566ff35c6.html|title=House committees request new closed-door impeachment testimony from U.S. official in Ukraine|website=Axios}}</ref> Holmes' statement provided the first testimony under oath that Trump directly and contemporaneously requested investigations of Joe and Hunter Biden and Burisma, with Trump allegedly asking "so he's gonna do the investigation?", refuting the potential defense that Trump had not been involved, and that Sondland might have been acting without the president's knowledge.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://slate.com/news-and-politics/2019/11/david-holmes-confirms-trump-asked-about-ukraine-investigation.html|title=Aide Confirms Trump Asked About Ukraine Investigation, Delivering Blow to GOP Defense|last=Politi|first=Daniel|date=November 16, 2019|website=Slate Magazine|language=en|access-date=November 18, 2019}}</ref> Further, Holmes' deposition raised questions about the credibility, accuracy, and truthfulness of Ambassador Sondland's previous sworn deposition, furthering the possibility that Sondland either perjured himself or needed to clarify his original sworn statement.<ref>{{cite news |first=Fadel |last=Allassan |date=November 16, 2019 |url=https://www.axios.com/david-holmes-confirms-trump-asked-sondland-ukraine-investigation-4c20f887-d79d-4bc4-8c73-d4fdc0dc91ce.html|title=State Department official confirms Trump asked Sondland about Ukraine investigation|website=Axios|access-date=November 18, 2019}}</ref> Third, Holmes' statement provided the first characterization of the actual language and degree of Trump's interest in having Ukraine investigate the Bidens, with Sondland saying to Trump about Zelensky that "he loves your ass" and "will do anything you ask him to", and Sondland later telling Holmes that President Trump "doesn't give a shit about Ukraine" and "only cares about the big stuff"—namely, investigations into the Bidens.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.cbsnews.com/news/david-holmes-statement-impeachment-inquiry-full-opening-statement/ |date=November 12, 2019 |title=Read David Holmes' full opening statement in impeachment inquiry|website=CBS News|language=en-US|access-date=November 18, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.msnbc.com/the-beat-with-ari/watch/-it-s-a-bombshell-shakedown-witness-confirms-damning-impeachment-call-73563205693|title='It's a bombshell': Shakedown witness confirms damning impeachment call|website=MSNBC|language=en|access-date=November 18, 2019}}</ref>

The phone call being made in a public restaurant in Kyiv on unencrypted cell phones with [[Foreign Intelligence Service (Russia)|Russian intelligence]] agents potentially listening to the conversation raised security concerns to some former diplomats and military officials.<ref name="CNN Kyiv call">{{Cite web|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/14/politics/bill-taylor-gordon-sondland-call-trump-security-concerns/index.html|title=Russian spies likely intercepted ambassador's cell phone call with Trump|last=Cohen|first=Zachary|last2=Collier|first2=Kevin|date=November 14, 2019|website=CNN|access-date=December 6, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.seattletimes.com/nation-world/sondlands-cellphone-call-to-trump-from-kyiv-restaurant-was-a-stunning-breach-of-security-former-officials-say/ |first=Ellen |last=Nakashima |title=Sondland's cellphone call to Trump from Kyiv restaurant was a stunning breach of security, former officials say|date=November 13, 2019|website=The Seattle Times|language=en-US|access-date=December 6, 2019}}</ref><ref name="MSNBC Kyiv call">{{Cite news |date=November 16, 2019 |url=https://www.msnbc.com/am-joy/watch/trump-sondland-call-posed-danger-to-u-s-national-security-and-foreign-policy-experts-say-73595973549|title=Trump–Sondland call posed danger to U.S. national security and foreign policy, experts say|website=MSNBC.com|language=en|access-date=December 6, 2019}}</ref><ref name="unencrypted security concerns">{{Cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/national-security/phone-logs-in-impeachment-report-renew-concern-about-security-of-trump-communications/2019/12/05/2066fbf4-16fe-11ea-8406-df3c54b3253e_story.html|title=Phone logs in impeachment report renew concern about security of Trump communications|last=Sonne|first=Paul|last2=Dawsey|first2=Josh|date=December 5, 2019|website=The Washington Post|language=en|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191206084259/https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/national-security/phone-logs-in-impeachment-report-renew-concern-about-security-of-trump-communications/2019/12/05/2066fbf4-16fe-11ea-8406-df3c54b3253e_story.html|archive-date=December 6, 2019|access-date=December 6, 2019|last3=Nakashima|first3=Ellen|last4=Miller|first4=Greg}}</ref> The circumstances of the call, along with later subpoenaed phone records included in the House Intelligence Committee's impeachment inquiry report, which also appeared to be unencrypted, led John Sipher, former deputy chief of Russia operations for the [[Central Intelligence Agency|CIA]], to comment to the Washington Post that Trump and Giuliani have effectively "given the Russians ammunition they can use in an overt fashion, a covert fashion or in the twisting of information".<ref name="unencrypted security concerns" /> He continued "Congress and investigators have call records that suggest certain things but have no means whatsoever of getting the actual text [of what was said]. I guarantee the Russians have the actual information."

On November 16, OMB official Mark Sandy was deposed.<ref name=sandydeposition>{{cite news |first=Zachary |last=Basu |date=November 15, 2019 |url=https://www.axios.com/white-house-budget-official-testify-impeachment-inquiry-79606799-5e37-4470-9daf-a347e56c0124.html|title=White House budget official will testify in impeachment inquiry if subpoenaed|website=Axios}}</ref> In his deposition, Sandy acknowledged that Trump did enact an unusual freeze in aid to Ukraine.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/16/politics/mark-sandy-deposition-impeachment-inquiry/index.html|title=WH budget official lays out unusual process in freeze of Ukraine aid for impeachment investigators |date=November 17, 2019 |first1=Manu |last1=Raju |first2=Lauren |last2=Fox |first3=Phil |last3=Mattingly |first4=Veronica |last4=Stracqualursi|website=CNN}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.startribune.com/impeachment-testimony-comes-from-white-house-budget-official/565036632/ |title=Testimony ties president closer to pressure on Ukraine |website=Star Tribune |first=Lisa |last=Mascaro |first2=Mary Clare |last2=Jalonic |first3=Michael |last3=Balsamo |agency=AP |date=November 16, 2019}}</ref> Sandy testified that two OMB employees had recently resigned while expressing concerns about the [[Impoundment Control Act of 1974|Impoundment Control Act]] hold on aid to Ukraine.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/us-policy/2019/11/26/two-omb-officials-resigned-voicing-concerns-over-ukraine-aid-hold-official-testifies/|title=Two OMB officials resigned voicing concerns over Ukraine aid hold, official testifies|last=Werner|first=Erica|date=November 26, 2019|website=Washington Post|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191126235107/https://www.washingtonpost.com/us-policy/2019/11/26/two-omb-officials-resigned-voicing-concerns-over-ukraine-aid-hold-official-testifies/|archive-date=November 26, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://thehill.com/homenews/house/472207-state-dept-official-describes-frantic-effort-to-save-recalled-ukraine|title=State Dept. official describes frantic effort to save recalled Ukraine ambassador|last=Byrnes|first=Jesse|date=November 26, 2019|website=The Hill|language=en|access-date=November 27, 2019}}</ref>

=== Resolution to begin public hearings ===

On October 29, 2019, Representative [[Jim McGovern (American politician)|Jim McGovern]] (D-Massachusetts) introduced a resolution ([https://www.congress.gov/116/bills/hres660/BILLS-116hres660rh.pdf H. Res. 660]), referred to House Rules Committee, which set forth the "format of open hearings in the House Intelligence Committee, including staff-led questioning of witnesses, and [authorization for] the public release of deposition transcripts".<ref name="FA Res Oct 30">{{cite web |url=https://foreignaffairs.house.gov/2019/10/four-chairs-statement-on-resolution-for-open-hearings-on-trump-s-abuse-of-power |title=Four Chairs Statement on Resolution for Open Hearings on Trump's Abuse of Power |website=House Foreign Affairs Committee |language=en|access-date=October 30, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.cbsnews.com/live-news/trump-impeachment-inquiry-latest-alexander-vindman-to-testify-2019-10-29/ |title=House Democrats unveil impeachment resolution—live updates |last=Segers |first=Grace |last2=Watson |first2=Kathryn |date=October 29, 2019 |website=CBS News |language=en-US |access-date=October 30, 2019 |last3=Tillett |first3=Emily |last4=Becket |first4=Stefan}}</ref> It also proposed the procedures for the transfer of evidence to House Judiciary Committee as it considers articles of impeachment.<ref name="FA Res Oct 30" /><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://time.com/5712533/house-democrats-impeachment-resolution/ |title=House Democrats Will Vote on Impeachment Inquiry Resolution Thursday |last=Abramson |first=Alana |date=October 28, 2019 |website=Time |language=en-US |access-date=October 30, 2019}}</ref> The resolution was debated in Rules Committee the next day and brought to a floor vote on October 31.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/congress/republicans-slam-dems-committee-readies-impeachment-resolution-floor-vote-n1074231 |title=GOP slams Dems as committee readies impeachment resolution for floor vote |last=Clark |first=Dartunorro |date=October 30, 2019 |website=NBC News |language=en-US |access-date=October 31, 2019}}</ref> It was adopted with a vote of 232 to 196, with two Democrats and all Republicans voting against the measure.<ref name="auto4"/>
