On November 4, 2019, two transcripts of the closed-door depositions, those of Ambassadors Yovanovitch and McKinley, were released by the three presiding House committees.<ref>{{Cite report |url=https://intelligence.house.gov/news/documentsingle.aspx?DocumentID=757 |title=Committees Release Testimony of Yovanovitch and Mckinley as Part of New Public Phase of Impeachment Inquiry |date=November 4, 2019 |publisher=Permanent Select Committee on Intelligence|access-date=November 5, 2019}}</ref><ref name="first transcripts">{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/congress/panels-release-first-transcripts-from-closed-door-interviews/2019/11/04/6ad4ea60-ff26-11e9-8341-cc3dce52e7de_story.html |title=Former U.S. envoy says she was warned she was being targeted |last=Jalonick |first=Mary Clare |last2=Tucker |first2=Eric |date=November 4, 2019 |work=The Washington Post |language=en-US |access-date=November 5, 2019 |last3=Mascaro |first3=Lisa}}</ref><ref name="excerpts and analysis nov. 4">{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/11/04/us/politics/house-intelligence-committee-transcripts-released.html |title=Impeachment Inquiry Transcripts: Excerpts and Analysis |date=November 4, 2019 |work=The New York Times|access-date=November 5, 2019 |language=en-US |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> The transcripts revealed that Yovanovitch first learned, from Ukrainian officials in November or December 2018, of a campaign by Giuliani and Lutsenko to remove her from her post.<ref name="excerpts and analysis nov. 4" /> Yovanovitch also testified that the U.S. embassy in Ukraine denied a visa application from the former Ukrainian prosecutor Viktor Shokin "to visit family" in the U.S. Although the application was simply denied because of his corrupt dealings in Ukraine, the ambassador later learned he had lied on his application and that the true purpose of the visit was to meet with Giuliani and "provide information about corruption at the embassy, including my [alleged] corruption", she told the committees. Giuliani lobbied the [[Assistant Secretary of State for Consular Affairs|assistant secretary for consular affairs]], conceding the true purpose of Shokin's planned visit to the U.S. The State Department meanwhile remained silent while she faced public attacks in an attempt to recall her to the U.S.<ref name="excerpts and analysis nov. 4" /> Yovanovitch had been told by Sondland that showing support for the U.S. president may help prevent her dismissal but she chose not to heed the advice.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/11/04/takeaways-marie-yovanovitchs-an-michael-mckinleys-ukraine-testimony/ |title=7 takeaways from Marie Yovanovitch's and Michael McKinley's Ukraine testimony |last=Blake |first=Aaron |last2=Phillips |first2=Amber |date=November 4, 2019 |work=The Washington Post |language=en-US |access-date=November 5, 2019}}</ref><ref name="excerpts and analysis nov. 4" />

McKinley, a former ambassador and later senior adviser to Secretary Pompeo, testified that he had three times advised the Secretary of State to defend Yovanovitch after the July 25 call in which Trump disparaged her became public knowledge. McKinley also said Kent was being pressured by State Department lawyers to remain silent and that Kent feared the State Department was relaying inaccurate information to Congress.<ref name="excerpts and analysis nov. 4" /> McKinley told the committees: "To see the emerging information on the engagement of our missions to procure negative political information for domestic purposes, combined with the failure I saw in the [State Department] to provide support for our professional cadre in a particularly trying time, I think the combination was a pretty good reason to decide enough, that I had no longer a useful role to play."<ref name="first transcripts" />

Transcripts of the depositions of Ambassadors Volker and Sondland were released on November 5, 2019.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/trump-impeachment-inquiry-live-updates/2019/11/05/a27d7c48-ff4e-11e9-8bab-0fc209e065a8_story.html |title=Live updates: Two more transcripts expected to be made public in Trump impeachment inquiry; GOP considers adding Jordan to intelligence panel |last=Wagner |first=John |date=November 5, 2019 |work=The Washington Post|access-date=November 6, 2019 |last2=Itkowitz |first2=Colby}}</ref> The transcript of Sondland's deposition on October 17 included an addendum filed by the ambassador on November 4.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.cbsnews.com/live-news/trump-impeachment-sondland-transcript-live-updates-2019-11-06/ |title=Top diplomat changes story on Ukraine aid—live updates |last=Segers |first=Grace |last2=Watson |first2=Kathryn |date=November 6, 2019 |website=CBS News |language=en-US |access-date=November 6, 2019 |last3=Becket |first3=Stefan}}</ref> In the addendum, he said he had "refreshed [his] recollection" having now reviewed the testimonies of Taylor and Morrison which contradicted his original testimony. Sondland had originally claimed he "never" believed there were any preconditions for the release of military aid to Ukraine and that he "was dismayed when it was held up", but "didn't know why".<ref name="Sondland updates quid pro quo">{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/11/05/us/politics/impeachment-trump.html |title=Sondland Updates Impeachment Testimony, Describing Ukraine Quid Pro Quo |last=Schmidt |first=Michael S. |date=November 5, 2019 |work=The New York Times|access-date=November 6, 2019 |language=en-US}}</ref> In his new four-page sworn statement published along with the transcripts, Sondland confirmed that he had told President Zelensky's aide, Yermak, during a meeting on September 1, that the release of aid was predicated on the Ukrainian president's committing to an investigation of Burisma.<ref name="Sondland updates quid pro quo" /><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/national-security/with-revised-testimony-sondland-ties-trump-to-quid-pro-quo/2019/11/05/3059b3b8-ffec-11e9-9518-1e76abc088b6_story.html |title=With revised statement, Sondland adds to testimony linking aid to Ukraine investigations that Trump sought |last=Harris |first=Shane |last2=Davis |first2=Aaron C. |date=November 5, 2019 |work=The Washington Post |language=en-US |access-date=November 6, 2019}}</ref>

The transcript of Ambassador Taylor's deposition was also released on November 6. During his deposition on October 22, he described the campaign, led by Giuliani, to instigate investigations into the Bidens in Ukraine. Taylor said it was his "clear understanding, security assistance money would not come until the [Ukrainian] president committed to pursue the investigation".<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/11/06/us/politics/trump-impeachment-hearings.html |title=Top Ukraine Diplomat Testified Giuliani Spearheaded Pressure for Investigations |last=Fandos |first=Nicholas |date=November 6, 2019 |work=The New York Times |access-date=November 7, 2019 |language=en-US |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> The following day saw the release of Kent's testimony transcripts in which he said, "[President Trump] wanted nothing less than President Zelensky to go to a microphone and say investigations, Biden and Clinton".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/national-security/trumps-demands-of-ukraine-came-down-to-three-words-investigations-biden-and-clinton-officials-testimony-shows/2019/11/07/d5ffab54-0197-11ea-8bab-0fc209e065a8_story.html|title=Trump's demands of Ukraine came down to three words: 'Investigations, Biden and Clinton', official's testimony states|last=Jaffe|first=Greg|last2=DeBonis|first2=Mike|date=November 7, 2019|website=Washington Post|language=en|access-date=November 12, 2019}}</ref>

Following public release of the transcripts, Trump asserted they had been "doctored" by Schiff and encouraged Republicans to "put out their own transcripts!"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2019/nov/11/trump-impeachment-inquiry-democrats-accusation-transcripts|title=Trump accuses Democrats of 'doctored' inquiry transcripts without evidence|last=Smith|first=David|date=November 11, 2019|website=The Guardian|access-date=November 11, 2019}}</ref>

== Related judicial proceedings ==

{{see|Trump v. Deutsche Bank, AG|Trump v. Mazars USA, LLP}}

=== ''Kupperman v. House of Representatives'' ===

On October 25, 2019, Charles Kupperman, Trump's former deputy national security adviser, filed an advisory lawsuit, asking a D.C. federal judge to rule on whether he is lawfully obliged to comply with a subpoena he received from the House of Representatives. He said he will follow whatever the judge says.<ref name="kupperman1" /> He was scheduled to testify on October 28 but did not appear. On October 31, Judge [[Richard J. Leon]] scheduled a hearing for December 10.<ref name="impeachment before subpoena" /> On November 6, the House joint investigating committees dropped their subpoena of Kupperman, asking that the parties abide by the ruling in a similar lawsuit pending against [[Don McGahn]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/local/legal-issues/charles-kupperman-subpoena-withdrawn-by-house-as-it-asks-judge-to-dismiss-lawsuit-over-his-testimony/2019/11/06/2fa9f426-00d9-11ea-9518-1e76abc088b6_story.html|title=Charles Kupperman subpoena withdrawn by House as it asks judge to dismiss lawsuit over his testimony|last=Marimow|first=Ann E.|last2=Hsu|first2=Spencer S.|date=November 6, 2019|website=The Washington Post|language=en|access-date=November 22, 2019}}</ref> Judge Leon indicated that the suit will go on anyway.<ref name = continue>{{cite news|url=https://talkingpointsmemo.com/muckraker/kupperman-case-house-moot-on-track-subpoena|title=Judge Won't End Fight Over Impeachment Subpoena Even After House Dems Back Down|last=Sneed|first=Tierney|date=November 7, 2019|work=Talking Points Memo|accessdate=November 11, 2019}}</ref>

On November 9, former national security advisor John Bolton, who had joined in the Kupperman lawsuit, had his lawyer send a [[proffer]] to the committees, saying he could supply much additional pertinent information the committee did not have.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/08/politics/john-bolton-lawyer-ukraine-information/|title=Bolton's lawyer says he has information on Ukraine that hasn't been disclosed|last1=Cohen|first1=Zachary|last2=de Vogue|first2=Ariane|date=November 8, 2019|work=CNN|accessdate=November 11, 2019}}</ref> White House acting chief of staff Mick Mulvaney also attempted to join in the Kupperman lawsuit.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/09/politics/mick-mulvaney-subpoena-lawsuit/index.html|title=Mulvaney tries to join a lawsuit fighting House subpoena power|last=Polantz|first=Katelyn|date=November 10, 2019|work=CNN|accessdate=November 11, 2019}}</ref> On November 11, Bolton's attorney filed a motion to block Mulvaney from joining the suit, arguing that Mulvaney had effectively waived immunity by acknowledging a ''quid pro quo'' in the Ukraine matter during an October 17 press briefing.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/11/11/us/politics/bolton-mulvaney-impeachment.html|title=Bolton Rejects Legal Alliance With Mulvaney|first=Peter|last=Baker|date=November 11, 2019|work=The New York Times}}</ref> Kupperman also objected to Mulvaney's participation and the judge said he was inclined not to allow it, whereupon Mulvaney withdrew his request.<ref>{{cite news |first=Josh |last=Gerstein |first2=Darren |last2=Samuelsohn |first3=Kyle |last3=Cheney |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/11/11/bolton-deputy-mulvaney-impeachment-lawsuit-069309|title=Mick Mulvaney withdraws attempt to join suit over impeachment testimony|date=November 11, 2019|work=Politico|accessdate=November 12, 2019}}</ref>

There were oral arguments on December 10,<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.npr.org/2019/12/10/786893630/lawyer-bolton-aide-charles-kupperman-fears-house-will-reissue-subpoena-for-testi|title=Lawyer: Bolton Aide Charles Kupperman Fears House Will Reissue Subpoena For Testimony|website=[[NPR]] |date=December 10, 2019 |first=Bobby |last=Allyn}}</ref> and the case was dismissed on December 30, 2019.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://thehill.com/regulation/court-battles/476297-judges-tosses-suit-over-impeachment-testimony-of-former-bolton-aide|title=Judge tosses suit over impeachment testimony of former Bolton aide|first=Regina|last=Zilbermints|date=December 30, 2019|website=TheHill}}</ref>

=== ''In re: Don McGahn'' ===

{{Main|In re: Don McGahn}}
{{see|Mueller Report#House Judiciary Committee}}
[[File:U.S. House Judiciary Committee v. Donald F. McGahn D.C. District Court Memorandum Opinion.pdf|thumb|upright|D.C. District Court ruling ordering Don McGahn to follow a Congressional subpoena to appear before the House Judiciary Committee]]

U.S. District Court Judge [[Ketanji Brown Jackson]] presided over a case to decide whether or not the House Judiciary Committee can enforce a subpoena against former White House counsel Don McGahn.<ref name="Politico ruling date">{{cite news |date=November 19, 2019 |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/11/19/impeachment-mcgahn-subpoena-071653| title=Judge will rule by Nov. 25 in Don McGahn subpoena fight |first=Darren |last=Samuelsohn |website=[[Politico]]}}</ref> The House Judiciary Committee wants his testimony on matters related to Robert Mueller's report that certain actions could constitute obstruction of justice. The Justice Department had claimed "absolute immunity". On November 25 she ruled that he must testify, declaring that "no one is above the law," but that he could invoke executive privilege on certain questions.<ref name="nprnov25">{{cite news|url=https://www.npr.org/2019/11/25/782705643/federal-judge-rules-that-mcgahn-must-testify-delivering-blow-to-white-house|title=Federal Judge Rules That McGahn Must Testify, Delivering Blow To White House|last=Allyn|first=Bobby|date=November 25, 2019|accessdate=November 25, 2019|publisher=NPR}}</ref><ref name="Pacer McGahn">{{Cite web| url=https://www.pacermonitor.com/public/case/29458255/COMMITTEE_ON_THE_JUDICIARY_OF_THE_US_HOUSE_OF_REPRESENTATIVES_v_MCGAHN_II|title=COMMITTEE ON THE JUDICIARY OF THE U.S. HOUSE OF REPRESENTATIVES v. MCGAHN II (1:19-cv-02379), District Of Columbia District Court|website=pacermonitor.com|access-date=December 8, 2019}}</ref> Jackson's ruling said that the Justice Department's claim to "unreviewable absolute testimonial immunity" is "baseless, and as such, cannot be sustained".<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/local/legal-issues/former-white-house-counsel-donald-mcgahn-must-comply-with-house-subpoena-judge-rules/2019/11/25/6de26cc8-018d-11ea-8bab-0fc209e065a8_story.html|title=Former White House counsel Donald McGahn must comply with House subpoena, judge rules|last=Hsu|first=Spencer S.|date=November 26, 2019|website=The Washington Post|language=en|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191126010212/https://www.washingtonpost.com/local/legal-issues/former-white-house-counsel-donald-mcgahn-must-comply-with-house-subpoena-judge-rules/2019/11/25/6de26cc8-018d-11ea-8bab-0fc209e065a8_story.html|archive-date=November 26, 2019|access-date=December 10, 2019}}</ref>

Excerpts from the ruling include:

* "When DOJ insists that presidents can lawfully prevent their senior-level aides from responding to compelled congressional process and that neither the federal courts nor Congress has the power to do anything about it, DOJ promotes a conception of separation-of-powers principles that gets these constitutional commands exactly backwards. In reality, it is a core tenet of this Nation's founding that the powers of a monarch must be split between the branches of the government to prevent tyranny."<ref name="McGahn appeal">{{Cite news |url=https://www.axios.com/don-mcgahn-house-subpoena-ruling-trump-impeachment-dba4db98-6d91-4861-a6bc-2f7c66ba5ee5.html|title=McGahn appeals ruling ordering him to comply with House impeachment subpoena|website=Axios|language=en|access-date=December 6, 2019}}</ref>
* "Stated simply, the primary takeaway from the past 250 years of recorded American history is that presidents are not kings. See ''[[Federalist No. 51|The Federalist No. 51]]'' (James Madison); ''[[Federalist No. 69|The Federalist No. 69]]'' (Alexander Hamilton); 1{{nbsp}}Alexis de Tocqueville, ''[[Democracy in America]]'' 115–18 (Harvey C. Mansfield & Delba Winthrop eds. & trans., Univ. of Chicago Press 2000) (1835)."<ref name="Judiciary v. McGahn" />{{Rp|114}}
* "In this land of liberty, it is indisputable that current and former employees of the White House work for the People of the United States, and that they take an oath to protect and defend the Constitution of the United States."<ref name="Judiciary v. McGahn" />{{Rp|114}}
* "To be sure, there may well be circumstances in which certain aides of the President possess confidential, classified, or privileged information that cannot be divulged in the national interest and that such aides may be bound by statute or executive order to protect. But, in this Court's view, the withholding of such information from the public square in the national interest and at the behest of the President is a duty that the aide herself possesses."<ref name="Judiciary v. McGahn" />{{Rp|114}}
* "DOJ's present assertion that the absolute testimonial immunity that senior-level presidential aides possess is, ultimately, owned by the President, and can be invoked by the President to overcome the aides' own will to testify, is a proposition that cannot be squared with core constitutional values, and for this reason alone, it cannot be sustained."<ref name="Judiciary v. McGahn" />{{Rp|114–115}}
* The United States of America has a government of laws and not of men.<ref name="Judiciary v. McGahn">{{Cite web|url=https://ecf.dcd.uscourts.gov/cgi-bin/show_public_doc?2019cv2379-46|title=Committee on the Judiciary, United States House of Representatives v. Donald F. McGahn II|date=Nov 25, 2019|website=uscourts.gov|access-date=December 5, 2019}}</ref>{{Rp|116}}

The administration has appealed the ruling.<ref name="McGahn appeal" /> Reacting on Twitter, McGahn attorney William Burck said McGahn will comply unless the order is stayed pending appeal,<ref name="NBC McGahn ruling">{{cite news|url=https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/trump-impeachment-inquiry/former-white-house-counsel-don-mcgahn-must-obey-subpoena-testify-n1090566|title=Former White House counsel Don McGahn must obey subpoena to testify before Congress, judge rules|last=Williams|first=Pete|date=November 25, 2019|work=NBC News|accessdate=November 25, 2019}}</ref> and on November 26 the Department of Justice asked Jackson to put a temporary [[Stay of execution|stay]] on her order so they can appeal it.<ref name="McGahn Appeal DoJ">{{cite news|url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/11/26/doj-moves-to-halt-judges-ruling-that-mcgahn-must-testify-073923|title=DOJ moves to halt judge's ruling that McGahn must testify|last=Samuelsohn|first=Darren|date=November 26, 2019|work=Politico|accessdate=November 26, 2019}}</ref> A one-week stay was granted, and when the lawyers asked for a second stay on December 2, it was denied.<ref name="Politico stay denied">{{cite news |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/12/02/judge-denies-doj-request-don-mcgahn-074846 |first=Darren |last=Samuelsohn |first2=Josh |last2=Gerstein |title=Judge denies DOJ request for stay on Don McGahn testimony|date=December 2, 2019|work=Politico|accessdate=December 4, 2019}}</ref>

=== Request for Grand Jury materials ===

House Democrats have requested the records from the grand jury proceedings that were part of the [[Mueller investigation]], stating that the material was needed to investigate whether or not articles of impeachment should include perjury charges against the president based on his responses to the Mueller probe. The district court decided in their favor, but two of the three judges on an appeals court panel seemed skeptical. They set oral arguments for January 3, 2020.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/11/18/court-mueller-russia-probe-071351|title=Judges suggest court shouldn't solve dispute over Mueller's evidence|last=Samuelsohn|first=Darren|last2=Gerstein|first2=Josh|date=November 18, 2019|website=Politico}}</ref> On March 10, 2020 the panel ruled 2–1 in favor of releasing the material to Congress.<ref>{{cite news |first=Katelyn |last=Polantz |date=March 10, 2020 |work=CNN |accessdate=August 19, 2020 |url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/03/10/politics/house-mueller-secret-grand-jury/index.html |title=House wins access to Mueller grand jury details, appeals court rules }}</ref>

On January 3, lawyers for the [[United States House Committee on the Judiciary|House Judiciary Committee]] urged the court to enforce the subpoena against McGahn, arguing that McGahn's testimony could provide the basis for new articles of impeachment against the President.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://thehill.com/homenews/house/476651-house-lawyers-press-court-to-enforce-subpoena-against-trump-aide |title=House lawyers press court to enforce subpoena against Trump aide |first=John |last=Kruzel |work=The Hill |date=January 3, 2020 }}</ref> When Trump-appointed judges asked what might happen if the courts demurred, Letter raised the specter of chaos and civil war,<ref>{{Cite news |date=January 3, 2020 |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/local/legal-issues/in-clash-with-trump-administration-house-democrats-seek-secret-grand-jury-evidence-and-testimony-from-former-white-house-counsel-donald-mcgahn/2020/01/02/32b8f538-2d6e-11ea-bcb3-ac6482c4a92f_story.html|title=Appeals court grapples with wading into political fight over grand jury materials, McGahn testimony|first1=Ann E.|last1=Marimow|first2=Robert |last2=Barnes |website=Washington Post}}</ref> raising the prospect of a pitched gun battle between the Sergeant at arms and the attorney general'fs security detail.

=== Other proceedings ===

On November 22, the State Department released 100 pages of documents in response to a court order. The documents show that Giuliani and Pompeo spoke on the phone twice in late March, confirming a statement made by David Hale in his public testimony. They also show that Trump's then-assistant [[Madeleine Westerhout]] helped to put Giuliani in touch with Pompeo.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.foxnews.com/politics/impeachment-state-department-100-pages-documents-pompeo-giuliani-yovanovitch-sondland|title=Giuliani-Pompeo contacts before Yovanovitch ouster are seen in newly released State Dept. documents|last=Wallace|first=Danielle|date=November 23, 2019|work=Fox News|accessdate=November 23, 2019}}</ref> Pompeo also spoke with [[Devin Nunes]] a few days later.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/11/23/state-department-pompeo-giuliani-073064|title=State Dept. documents reveal contact between Pompeo and Giuliani|last=Choi|first=Matthew|date=November 23, 2019|work=Politico|accessdate=November 23, 2019}}</ref> Early the next month, six former Ukraine ambassadors wrote a letter to Pompeo objecting to "recent uncorroborated allegations" against then-ambassador Marie Yovanovitch, saying "these charges are simply wrong."<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/trump-impeachment-inquiry/documents-released-ethics-group-show-giuliani-pompeo-contacts-ukraine-ambassador-n1090091|title=Documents released to ethics group show Giuliani, Pompeo contacts before Ukraine ambassador ousted|last1=Helsel|first1=Phil|last2=Williams|first2=Abigail|date=November 23, 2019|work=NBC News|accessdate=November 23, 2019}}</ref>

Other FOIA requests have been made in related cases.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://thehill.com/regulation/471932-judge-orders-pentagon-budget-office-to-give-ukraine-documents-to-news-outlet|title=Judge orders Pentagon, budget office to give Ukraine documents to news outlet|first=Brandon|last=Conradis|date=November 25, 2019|website=The Hill}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.huffpost.com/entry/judge-pentagon-white-house-budget-office-records-ukraine-aid_n_5ddc8c07e4b0d50f32958796|title=Judge Orders Pentagon, White House Budget Office To Release Records On Ukraine Aid|first=Sanjana|last=Karanth|date=November 25, 2019|website=HuffPost}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://drive.google.com/file/d/1k25C0_ydlrxyiH-CfhzymqsGuIN8iMkX/view?usp=embed_facebook|title=CKKopinion.pdf|website=Google Docs}}</ref>

On November 6, 2019, Chairman [[Adam Schiff]] announced that the first public hearings of the impeachment inquiry would be held on November 13, beginning with Bill Taylor and George Kent.<ref name=beginning>{{cite web |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/state-department-official-to-testify-in-impeachment-probe-11573038000 |title=First Public Hearings in Impeachment Inquiry to Begin Next Week |last=Volz |first=Dustin |last2=Andrews |first2=Natalie |date=November 6, 2019 |website=The Wall Street Journal |language=en-US |access-date=November 7, 2019}}</ref> The announcement added that [[Marie Yovanovitch]] would testify in the second public hearing on November 15.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/11/06/house-democrats-will-hold-first-public-impeachment-hearings-next-week-000319 |title=First public impeachment hearings will take place next week |last=Desiderio |first=Andrew |last2=Cheney |first2=Kyle |date=November 6, 2019 |website=Politico |language=en-US |access-date=November 7, 2019}}</ref> The White House appointed new aides, including [[Pam Bondi]] and [[Tony Sayegh]], to work on communications during the inquiry.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/white-house-expected-to-bolster-impeachment-strategy-with-two-new-hires-11573068363 |title=White House Expected to Bolster Impeachment Strategy With Two New Hires |last=Bender |first=Michael C. |date=November 6, 2019 |work=The Wall Street Journal |access-date=November 6, 2019 |language=en-US}}</ref> House Republicans assigned Representative [[Jim Jordan (American politician)|Jim Jordan]] (R-Ohio) to the House Intelligence Committee to participate in the hearings. Jordan replaced Representative [[Rick Crawford (politician)|Rick Crawford]] (R-Arkansas), who stepped down so Jordan could take his place.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/11/08/jim-jordan-intelligence-committee-068049|title=Jim Jordan joins Intelligence Committee to boost Trump in public impeachment hearings|last=Zanona|first=Melanie|date=November 8, 2019|website=Politico|language=en-US|access-date=November 9, 2019}}</ref>

Per the House of Representatives resolution adopted in October 2019, Republican representatives can subpoena witnesses only with the concurrence of the Democratic committee chairman or with approval of the majority members.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Brune |first1=Tom |title=Nixon, Clinton, Trump: How the impeachment resolutions compare |url=https://www.newsday.com/news/nation/impeachment-resolutions-trump-nixon-clinton-1.38384184 |accessdate=November 11, 2019 |work=Newsday |date=November 9, 2019}}</ref> The House Intelligence Committee ranking member, Representative [[Devin Nunes]] (R-California), in a November{{nbsp}}9 letter, provided a list of eight witnesses from whom the minority party wished to hear, including Hunter Biden. In Schiff's decline of the request to hear from Biden, he said he would not allow Republicans to use the hearings to conduct "sham investigations".<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/11/09/us/politics/republican-strategy-impeachment-trump.html|title=Republicans Argue Impeachment Case Falls Short of Proving Trump Misconduct|first1=Michael D.|last1=Shear|first2=Nicholas|last2=Fandos|date=November 9, 2019|newspaper=The New York Times}}</ref> Schiff also rejected Nunes's request to question the anonymous whistleblower, for the individual's safety and because subsequent evidence "not only confirms but far exceeds" the whistleblower's complaint, so "the whistleblower's testimony is therefore redundant and unnecessary".<ref>{{cite news |date=November 10, 2019 |url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/09/politics/adam-schiff-whistleblower-impeachment-inquiry/index.html|title=Schiff says whistleblower testimony is 'redundant and unnecessary'|first=Manu|last=Raju|website=CNN}}</ref>

As public hearings approached, a staff memo to Republican members of the three relevant committees outlined the major themes they should pursue in Trump's defense. This includes focusing on the July 25 call summary which they allege "shows no conditionality or evidence of pressure" and that both Presidents Trump and Zelensky have said there was no pressure. The memo contended that any concerns Zelensky may have had about negative consequences of publicly acknowledging he felt pressure from Trump were unwarranted.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.vox.com/policy-and-politics/2019/11/12/20961073/trump-impeachment-hearings-republican-testimony-strategy|title=A Republican memo details the party's impeachment inquiry defenses. They aren't very strong.|first=Sean|last=Collins|date=November 12, 2019|website=Vox}}</ref> The memo also claims that the "Ukrainian government was not aware of a hold on U.S. security assistance" before the July 25 call. It also points out that "President Trump met with President Zelensky and U.S. security assistance flowed to Ukraine in September 2019—both of which occurred without Ukraine investigating President Trump's political rivals."<ref name="GOP defense memo">{{cite web |date=November 12, 2019 |first=Zachary |last=Basu |first2=Jonathan |last2=Swan |url=https://www.axios.com/republicans-impeachment-defense-memo-b4f6eeeb-6dab-49ed-a8d2-48eb736cfd8f.html|title=Ahead of public hearings, GOP outlines theory of impeachment defense in memo to members|website=Axios}}</ref>

The release of the Ukraine aid came two days after the House Intelligence Committee was notified of the whistleblower complaint and opened an investigation,<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/11/11/us/politics/trump-ukraine-timeline.html|title=Key Dates at the Center of the Ukraine Matter|first1=Sharon|last1=LaFraniere|first2=Andrew E.|last2=Kramer|first3=Danny|last3=Hakim|date=November 11, 2019|work=The New York Times}}</ref> and two days after three House committees publicly announced an investigation into Giuliani's activities in Ukraine.<ref>{{cite news |date=September 9, 2019 |url=https://www.politico.com/story/2019/09/09/rudy-giuliani-ukraine-investigation-1486753 |title=House panels launch investigation into Giuliani's dealings with Ukraine|first=Caitlin|last=Oprysko|website=[[Politico]]}}</ref>

As hearings began, Schiff said Trump may have committed bribery, and House Speaker Pelosi joined him on November 14; bribery is specifically listed as an impeachable offense in the Constitution.<ref name="auto2" /><ref name=Budryk /><ref>{{cite web|first=Caleb |last=Ecarma |url=https://www.mediaite.com/tv/how-did-democrats-decide-on-bribery-as-trumps-impeachable-offense/|title=How Did Democrats Decide on 'Bribery' as Trump's Offense?|date=November 22, 2019|website=Mediaite|language=en|access-date=November 23, 2019}}</ref>

=== November 13, 2019: Kent and Taylor ===

With live coverage on television, public hearings began at 10:00&nbsp;a.m. [[Eastern Standard Time (North America)|EST]] on November 13, 2019, in which [[George P. Kent|George Kent]] and [[William B. Taylor Jr.|William Taylor]] testified before the House Intelligence Committee.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/impeachment-hearings-live-updates/2019/11/13/e974f486-057b-11ea-ac12-3325d49eacaa_story.html|title=Live updates: Trump asked E.U. ambassador about status of Ukrainian 'investigations', diplomat reveals in new testimony|last=Wagner|first=John|last2=Sonmez|first2=Felicia|date=November 13, 2019|website=The Washington Post|access-date=November 13, 2019}}</ref> After opening statements from Chairman Schiff and ranking member Representative [[Devin Nunes|Nunes]], Taylor and Kent read their openings statements. This was followed by questions from the Chairman and the majority counsel, [[Daniel S. Goldman]], and then by the Ranking Member and the minority counsel, [[Steve Castor]].<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/13/politics/who-are-dan-goldman-steve-castor-impeachment-lawyers/index.html|title=Staff lawyers to take star role in first hearings on impeachment|last=Rogers|first=Alex|date=November 13, 2019|website=CNN|access-date=November 13, 2019}}</ref>

Taylor testified that the day after the Trump–Zelensky phone call, one of his aides, David Holmes, overheard Sondland speaking to Trump via cellphone in a Kyiv restaurant, hearing the president refer to "the investigations".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/impeachment-hearings-begin-with-revelation-of-phone-call-implicating-trump-in-ukraine-scandal/2019/11/13/de8d21b8-063b-11ea-b17d-8b867891d39d_story.html |date=November 13, 2019 |title=Impeachment hearings begin with new evidence of phone call implicating Trump in Ukraine controversy|first1=Karoun|last1=Demirjian|website=The Washington Post}}</ref> Another diplomat, Suriya Jayanti, also overheard the call. Holmes testified behind closed doors on November 15 that he heard Trump ask, "so, he's gonna do the investigation?" to which Sondland replied, "he's gonna do it", adding that Zelensky would do "anything you ask him to". Holmes also testified that Sondland later told him that Trump "did not give a shit about Ukraine" and "only cared about the big stuff{{nbsp}}... that benefits the president like the Biden investigation that Mr. Giuliani was pushing."<ref>{{cite news |first=Veronica |last=Rocha |first2=Meg |last2=Wagner |url=https://www.cnn.com/politics/live-news/impeachment-hearing-11-15-19/index.html|title=Former U.S. Ambassador to Ukraine testifies: Live updates|date=November 15, 2019|website=CNN|accessdate=November 15, 2019}}</ref>

Analysts noted that the Sondland call itself constituted a major security breach, as it could have been intercepted by foreign intelligence services.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/national-security/ambassadors-cellphone-call-to-trump-from-kyiv-restaurant-was-a-stunning-breach-of-security-former-officials-say/2019/11/13/37d75752-0641-11ea-b17d-8b867891d39d_story.html|title=Ambassador's cellphone call to Trump from Kyiv restaurant was a stunning breach of security, former officials say|last=Nakashima|first=Ellen|date=November 13, 2019|website=The Washington Post|access-date=November 14, 2019}}</ref>

According to data from [[Nielsen Corporation|Nielsen]], the first day of hearings had 13,098,000 viewers tuning in on various cable and broadcast channels (not including PBS, {{nowrap|C-SPAN}}, and online streaming).<ref>{{cite news |last=Patten |first=Dominic |url=https://deadline.com/2019/11/impeachment-hearings-tv-ratings-donald-trump-fox-news-cnn-msnbc-1202786141/ |title=Impeachment Hearings Debut With 13M Viewers; Fox News Tops Cable & Broadcast |work=[[Deadline Hollywood]] |date=November 14, 2019 |accessdate=November 14, 2019}}</ref>

=== November 15, 2019: Yovanovitch ===

[[Marie Yovanovitch]]'s testimony began at 9:00&nbsp;a.m. EST and lasted six hours.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-impeachment-hearings-yovanovitch-testimony-updates-2019-11|title=Marie Yovanovitch took aim at Trump, Rudy Giuliani, and top brass at the State Department in damning testimony|first1=Sonam|last1=Sheth |first2=Eliza|last2=Relman|date=Nov 15, 2019|accessdate=Nov 16, 2019|work=Business Insider}}</ref> She directly contradicted the Republican theory that Ukraine had tried to undermine Trump in the 2016 elections. She said she had three contacts with Giuliani, not involving the current allegations, and did not know why he chose to attack and discredit her.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://abcnews.go.com/Politics/key-takeaways-testimony-ukraine-ambassador-marie-yovanovitch/story?id=67044743|title=5 key takeaways from testimony by former Ukraine Ambassador Marie Yovanovitch|last=Flaherty|first=Anne|date=November 15, 2019|work=ABC News|accessdate=November 15, 2019}}</ref> She said his allegations against her were false and that no one in the State Department believed them. She added that she was "shocked and devastated" when Trump disparaged her and said she was "going to go through some things" during his telephone call with Zelensky.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/15/politics/public-impeachment-hearings-day-2/index.html|title=Former U.S. ambassador to Ukraine tells impeachment inquiry she was 'shocked and devastated' after being removed from her post|last1=Herb|first1=Jeremy|last2=Raju|first2=Manu|date=November 15, 2019|work=CNN|accessdate=November 15, 2019}}</ref>

During her testimony, Trump berated her on Twitter, questioning her competence and saying the Ukrainian president had spoken unfavourably about her.<ref name="BBC Yovanovitch">{{cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-50428537|title=How a Trump tweet shook impeachment hearing|first=Anthony|last=Zurcher|date=November 15, 2019|accessdate=November 16, 2019|work=BBC News}}</ref> Chairman Schiff informed Yovanovitch of the tweet during the hearing; she said it was "very intimidating".<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-50436521|title=Trump impeachment inquiry: Envoy 'intimidated' by tweets during testimony|date=November 15, 2019|work=BBC News|accessdate=November 16, 2019}}</ref> Trump's behavior was labelled as [[witness intimidation]] by Democrats.<ref name="BBC Yovanovitch" /> [[Eric Swalwell]], who participated in questioning Yovanovitch during the hearing, said this could be laid out as a separate article of impeachment: "it's evidence of more obstruction".<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-trump-impeachment/trump-attacks-impeachment-witness-on-twitter-democrats-see-intimidation-idUSKBN1XP155 |title=Trump attacks impeachment witness on Twitter, Democrats see intimidation |work=Reuters |first=Susan |last=Cornwell |first2=Richard |last2=Cowan |first3=Patricia |last3=Zengerle |date=November 15, 2019|accessdate=November 16, 2019}}</ref>

=== November 19, 2019 ===
==== Vindman and Williams ====

Lieutenant Colonel [[Alexander Vindman]] testified in person before the U.S. House of Representatives.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/11/18/who-is-alexander-vindman-why-does-his-public-testimony-matter/|title=Who is Alexander Vindman and why does his public testimony matter?|work=The Washington Post|date=November 19, 2019|first=Amber|last=Phillips|accessdate=November 20, 2019}}</ref> In his testimony, Vindman said he had made a report to an intelligence official about what he heard during Trump's call with the Ukrainian President and felt what the President mentioned during the phone conversation was "improper".<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/11/19/impeachment-hearings-live-highlights-and-updates-071459|title=Election meddling, an 'improper' call, and twins: What we learned in Vindman and Williams' testimony|work=Politico|first1=Natasha|last1=Bertrand|first2=Quint|last2=Forgey|first3=Abbey|last3=Marshall|date=November 19, 2019|accessdate=November 20, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/lt-col-alexander-vindman-reveals-in-testimony-that-he-told-an-intelligence-official-about-trumps-call-with-ukrainian-leader/2019/11/19/61c46b16-0ae4-11ea-8397-a955cd542d00_story.html|title=Trump said his Ukraine call was 'perfect'. Impeachment witnesses testified otherwise.|first1=Karoun|last1=Demirjian|first2=Mike|last2=DeBonis|first3=Matt|last3=Zapotosky|accessdate=November 20, 2019|date=November 19, 2019|work=The Washington Post}}</ref> Testifying alongside Vindman was Vice President Mike Pence's chief European security adviser [[Jennifer Williams]]. Williams testified that when Zelensky was elected, Pence initially agreed to attend the inauguration if his schedule permitted, but that plan was cancelled when on May 13, Williams was informed that President Trump had decided Pence would not represent the U.S. at the inauguration in Ukraine after all.<ref>{{cite news |title=Read Jennifer Williams's Prepared Opening Statement From the Impeachment Hearing |work=[[The New York Times]] |date=November 19, 2019 |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/11/19/us/politics/williams-opening-statement-impeachment.html}}</ref> Williams testified that she listened to Trump's phone conversation with Zelensky and felt it was "unusual".<ref>{{cite news |first=Michael D. |last=Shear |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/11/19/us/politics/jennifer-williams.html|title=Who Is Jennifer Williams? Pence Aid Listened to Trump–Zelensky Call |date=November 19, 2019 |accessdate=November 20, 2019 |newspaper=The New York Times}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/11/19/trump-ukraine-scrutiny-officials-testimony-071395|title='Improper' and 'unusual': White House aides criticize Trump's Ukraine call|work=Politico|first1=Andrew|last1=Desiderio|first2=Kyle|last2=Cheney|date=November 19, 2019|accessdate=November 20, 2019}}</ref> Both Vindman and Williams acknowledged the Trump administration's interest in obtaining knowledge of the Burisma controversy as well.<ref name="penceukraine">{{cite news |first=Aaron |last=Blake |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/11/19/early-takeaways-alexander-vindmans-jennifer-williamss-testimony/|title=7 Takeaways From Tuesday's Impeachment Hearings|work=The Washington Post|date=November 19, 2019|accessdate=November 20, 2019}}</ref>

In questioning Vindman, Devin Nunes repeatedly demanded that he name all individuals to whom he had spoken. In a heated exchange, Vindman refused, and Schiff rebuked Nunes for trying to violate federally protected anonymity.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/video/national/trump-impeachment-hearings/vindman-refuses-to-name-intelligence-community-colleagues-or-whistleblower/2019/11/19/58a1acd3-a4ba-4a1f-9987-abb9e26d1e50_video.html |title=Vindman refuses to name intelligence community colleagues or whistleblower |work=The Washington Post |date=November 19, 2019 |access-date=November 20, 2019 |language=en}}</ref>

==== Volker and Morrison ====

At the request of Republicans, former U.S. Special Representative for Ukraine [[Kurt Volker]] and former National Security presidential adviser on Europe and Russia [[Tim Morrison (presidential advisor)|Tim Morrison]] gave public testimony before the House Intelligence Committee.<ref>{{cite news |first=Veronica |last=Rocha |first2=Meg |last2=Wagner |first3=Amanda |last3=Wills |accessdate=May 14, 2020 |url=https://www.cnn.com/politics/live-news/impeachment-hearing-11-19-19/h_fcef5e3a2b318f1fee6c3405a9b80d06|title=Morrison and Volker are the witnesses Republicans requested|date=November 19, 2019|website=CNN}}</ref> In his testimony, Volker recanted his deposition denial of seeing no indication that Trump had conditioned a White House meeting and military assistance for Ukraine on a promise from the country's president to investigate Trump's political rivals.<ref name="denialtorecant">{{cite news|url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/11/19/kurt-volker-public-impeachment-hearing-071566|first=Kyle|last=Cheney|title='I have learned many things': Kurt Volker revises Ukraine testimony|work=Politico|date=November 19, 2019|accessdate=November 19, 2019}}</ref> Asked why he recanted, Volker said "I have learned many things" since the previous closed-door hearing on October 3, 2019.<ref name="denialtorecant" /> During his testimony, Morrison said Sondland confirmed to him that there was indeed a ''quid pro quo'' for U.S. aid to Ukraine and that Sondland told him this following the September{{nbsp}}1 telephone conversation with Yermak.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.vox.com/policy-and-politics/2019/11/19/20973157/impeachment-hearings-morrison-quid-pro-quo-ukraine|first=Alex|last=Ward|title=One of the Republicans' witnesses confirmed a quid pro quo on TV|work=Vox|date=November 19, 2019|accessdate=November 19, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://theweek.com/speedreads/879534/former-nsc-official-tim-morrison-confirms-ukraine-quid-pro-quo-during-public-testimony |first=Catherine |last=Garcia |title=Former NSC official Tim Morrison confirms Ukraine quid pro quo during public testimony|work=The Week|date=November 19, 2019|accessdate=November 20, 2019}}</ref>

=== November 20, 2019 ===
==== Sondland ====

Ambassador to the European Union [[Gordon Sondland]] testified that he conducted his work with Giuliani at the "express direction of the president",<ref name="Edelman">{{cite news|url=https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/trump-impeachment-inquiry/6-things-we-learned-gordon-sondland-s-impeachment-testimony-so-n1086841|title=6 things we learned from Gordon Sondland's impeachment testimony|last=Edelman|first=Adam|date=November 20, 2019|work=NBC News|accessdate=November 20, 2019}}</ref> and that he understood a potential White House invitation for Zelensky to be contingent on Ukraine announcing investigations into the 2016 elections and Burisma.<ref name="FT1">{{cite news|url=https://www.ft.com/content/30e68c3b-31fd-3736-a55a-b23189da2db1|title=Trump seeks to distance himself from Sondland|date=November 20, 2019|work=Financial Times|accessdate=November 20, 2019}}</ref><ref name="Sondland NYT">{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/11/20/us/politics/impeachment-hearings.html|title=Impeachment Hearing Live Updates: Gordon Sondland Ties Trump to Ukraine Pressure Campaign|last=Baker|first=Peter|date=November 20, 2019|work=The New York Times|access-date=November 20, 2019|last2=Schmidt|first2=Michael S.|language=en-US|issn=0362-4331}}</ref> Sondland made clear that he believed Giuliani was leading a ''quid pro quo'' scheme to pressure Ukraine on the president's behalf.<ref name="Sondland followed orders" /> He said he personally informed Zelensky, before the July 25 phone call, that Zelensky would need to assure Trump he planned a thorough investigation.<ref name="CNN everyone in loop" /> He additionally stated that everyone in the administration "was in the loop", specifically naming John Bolton, Mike Pompeo, Ulrich Brechbuhl and Mike Pence, saying "they knew what they were doing and why."<ref name="CNN everyone in loop">{{cite news|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/20/politics/public-impeachment-hearing-day-4/index.html|title=Ambassador says 'everyone was in the loop' on pushing Ukrainians to investigate Bidens |first1=Jeremy |last1=Herb |first2=Manu |last2=Raju |date=November 21, 2019 |website=CNN |access-date=November 20, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |first=Philip |last=Ewing |first2=Brian |last2=Naylor |date=November 20, 2019 |url=https://www.npr.org/2019/11/20/778657263/watch-live-sondland-key-impeachment-witness-headlines-wednesday-hearing |title=Sondland Says Top Trump Officials Knew Of Push For Ukraine Investigations |website=NPR.org |accessdate=May 14, 2020 }}</ref> Sondland also said Trump had never directly told him that the aid package to Ukraine was related to the announcement of investigations, but that Sondland nevertheless believed it was.<ref name="Sondland NYT" /><ref name="Sondland followed orders">{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/11/20/us/politics/sondland-in-act-of-defiance-says-he-followed-trumps-orders-in-ukraine-pressure-scheme.html|title=Sondland, in Act of Defiance, Says He Followed Trump's Orders in Ukraine Pressure Scheme|last=Fandos|first=Nicholas|date=November 20, 2019|work=The New York Times|access-date=November 20, 2019|last2=Schmidt|first2=Michael S.|language=en-US|issn=0362-4331}}</ref>

Hours after Sondland's testimony, Pence's Chief of Staff [[Marc Short]] issued a statement denying Sondland's claim that Pence and Sondland discussed the alleged ''quid pro quo''. The denial stated the vice president "never had a conversation with Gordon Sondland about investigating the Bidens, Burisma, or the conditional release of financial aid to Ukraine based upon potential investigations".<ref>{{cite news |first=Kevin |last=Liptak |date=November 20, 2019  |url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/20/politics/mike-pence-ukraine-impeachment-gordon-sondland/index.html|title=Sondland testimony raises questions about Pence's denials on Ukraine|website=CNN|language=en|access-date=November 20, 2019}}</ref>

==== Cooper and Hale ====

[[Laura Cooper]], the deputy assistant secretary of defense for Russia, Ukraine, and Eurasia, testified that Ukrainian officials knew about the hold on military aid by July 25, the day of the Trump–Zelensky call, undercutting an assertion that there could not have been a ''quid pro quo'' because Ukraine was not aware of the hold.<ref>{{cite news |first=Meg |last=Wagner |first2=Veronica |last2=Rocha |first3=Amanda |last3=Wills |first4=Mike |last4=Hayes |first5=Fernando, III |last5=Alfonso |accessdate=May 14, 2020 |url=https://www.cnn.com/politics/live-news/impeachment-hearing-11-20-19/h_6caf4ca5223af63c44890ac182311825 |title=Pentagon official reveals Ukrainians asked about stalled aid as early as July|date=November 20, 2019|work=CNN}}</ref> [[David Hale (diplomat)|David Hale]], who serves as the [[United States Under Secretary of State for Political Affairs]], testified that he found out from an [[Office of Management and Budget|OMB]] official that aid to Ukraine was being withheld at the direction of Trump.<ref>{{cite news |first=Amber |last=Phillips |date=November 20, 2019 |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/11/20/takeaways-laura-coopers-david-hales-testimony-about-military-aid-ukraine/|title=3 takeaways from Laura Cooper's and David Hale's testimony|newspaper=The Washington Post}}</ref>

Late in the day, Trump praised the performance of Republicans during the hearings, declaring, "not only did we win today, it's over."<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.cbs42.com/top-stories/trump-declares-impeachment-inquiry-over/|title=Trump declares impeachment inquiry 'over'|date=November 20, 2019}}</ref>

=== November 21, 2019: Hill and Holmes ===

Fiona Hill—who until August 2019 was the top Russia expert on the NSC—criticized Republicans for promulgating the "fictional narrative" that Ukraine rather than Russia interfered in the 2016 election, asserting the theory was planted by Russia and played into its hands.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/11/21/us/politics/impeachment-hearing.html|title=Impeachment Inquiry Live Updates: Fiona Hill Denounces 'Fictional' Claim of Ukraine Meddling in 2016|first=Michael D.|last=Shear|date=November 21, 2019|work=The New York Times}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.pressherald.com/2019/11/21/todays-witnesses-will-cap-intense-week-in-impeachment-inquiry/ |title=Ex-White House aide undercuts Trump defense, saying Sondland did 'domestic political errand' |last1=Mascaro |first1=Lisa |first2=Mary Clare |last2=Jalonick |last3=Tucker |first3=Eric |agency=Associated Press |work=[[Portland Press Herald]] |date=November 22, 2019}}</ref> Testifying alongside Hill was the current head of political affairs in the U.S. Embassy in Ukraine, David Holmes, who said he was concerned about Giuliani's role in a campaign which involved attacking the ambassador to Ukraine, Marie Yovanovitch, as well as a push for Ukraine to investigate interference in the 2016 presidential election and the Bidens, and described Sondland, Volker and U.S. Energy Secretary Rick Perry as "The Three Amigos" who ran the Ukraine campaign with Trump and Giuliani.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.pbs.org/newshour/politics/witness-david-holmes-expresses-concerns-about-giulianis-role-in-ukraine|title=WATCH: Witness David Holmes expresses concerns about Giuliani's role in Ukraine |agency=Associated Press|work=PBS NewsHour|date=November 21, 2019|accessdate=November 21, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/11/21/david-holmes-made-clear-how-pressure-was-applied-ukraine-how-that-pressure-continues/ |date=November 21, 2019 |title=David Holmes made clear how pressure was applied to Ukraine—and how that pressure continues |first=Philip |last=Bump |website=[[The Washington Post]]}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |first=Amber |last=Phillips |date=November 21, 2019 |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/11/20/who-is-david-holmes-why-does-his-public-testimony-matter/|title=Who is David Holmes and why does his public testimony matter?|newspaper=The Washington Post |accessdate=May 14, 2020 }}</ref>

== Final report ==

[[File:20191203 - full report hpsci impeachment inquiry - 20191203.pdf|thumb|upright|"The Trump–Ukraine Impeachment Inquiry Report" released on December 3, 2019]]
[[File:2019-12-02-report-of-evidence-in-the-democrats-impeachment-inquiry-in-the-house-of-representatives.pdf|thumb|upright|Republican ''counter-report:'' "Report of Evidence In the Democrats' Impeachment Inquiry in the House of Representatives" released on December 2, 2019]]

On November 25, 2019, House Intelligence Committee Chairman Adam Schiff published a letter stating that next steps towards impeachment will be taken when a committee report regarding the impeachment inquiry will be sent to the House Judiciary Committee when Congress returns from its [[Thanksgiving]] recess.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/25/politics/adam-schiff-letter-impeachment-timeline/index.html|title=READ: Adam Schiff letter to lawmakers laying out path forward for impeachment inquiry|publisher=CNN|date=November 25, 2019|accessdate=November 25, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Wagner |first1=John |last2=Sonmez |first2=Felicia |last3=Brittany |first3=Shammas |title=Schiff says report will be forwarded to Judiciary Committee soon after Congress returns next week |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/live-impeachment-inquiry-updates/2019/11/25/0eabfc32-0f71-11ea-b0fc-62cc38411ebb_story.html |work=The Washington Post |accessdate=November 26, 2019 |date=November 25, 2019}}</ref>

A draft report was circulated among the membership of the House Intelligence Committee on December 2; the next day, it was released to the public.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/12/03/us/politics/impeachment-trump-intelligence-committee.html |title=Impeachment Report Alleges Trump Solicited Foreign Election Interference |last=Shear |first=Michael D. |date=December 3, 2019 |work=The New York Times |access-date=December 3, 2019 |last2=Fandos |first2=Nicholas |language=en-US |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> A [[Markup (legislation)|markup]] committee meeting took place, followed by a formal vote on its final text, and a vote on whether or not to send it to the Judiciary Committee.<ref>{{cite news |first=Bob |last=Brigham |url=https://www.rawstory.com/2019/11/intel-chairman-adam-schiff-announces-tuesday-vote-on-impeachment-inquiry-report-on-donald-trump/ |title=Intel Chairman Adam Schiff announces Tuesday vote on impeachment inquiry report on Donald Trump |publisher=Rawstory.com |date=November 30, 2019 |accessdate=December 4, 2019}}</ref> On December 3, the House Intelligence Committee voted 13–9 along party lines to adopt [https://intelligence.house.gov/report/ the report] and also send it to the House Judiciary Committee.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/12/03/politics/house-intelligence-committee-report/index.html|title=House Democrats vote to send impeachment report to Judiciary Committee|first1=Manu|last1=Raju|first2=Jeremy|last2=Herb|publisher=CNN|date=December 3, 2019|accessdate=December 4, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.foxnews.com/politics/house-intel-committee-trump-impeachment-report-vote|title=House Democrats vote to adopt Trump impeachment report, blast scheme to 'solicit foreign interference' in 2020 race|first1=Ronn|last1=Blitzer|first2=Gregg|last2=Re|publisher=Fox News|date=December 3, 2019|accessdate=December 4, 2019}}</ref><ref name="Intel-Report">{{Cite web|url=https://intelligence.house.gov/uploadedfiles/20191203_-_full_report___hpsci_impeachment_inquiry_-_20191203.pdf|title=Report of the House Permanent Select Committee on Intelligence, Pursuant to H. Res. 660 in Consultation with the House Committee on Oversight and Reform and the House Committee on Foreign Affairs|last=House Permanent Select Committee on Intelligence|date=December 3, 2019|website=U.S. House of Representatives Permanent Select Committee on Intelligence|access-date=December 5, 2019}}</ref>

The report's preface states:<blockquote>[T]he impeachment inquiry has found that President Trump, personally and acting through agents within and outside of the U.S. government, solicited the interference of a foreign government, Ukraine, to benefit his reelection. In furtherance of this scheme, President Trump conditioned official acts on a public announcement by the new Ukrainian President, Volodymyr Zelensky, of politically-motivated investigations, including one into President Trump's domestic political opponent. In pressuring President Zelensky to carry out his demand, President Trump withheld a White House meeting desperately sought by the Ukrainian President, and critical U.S. military assistance to fight Russian aggression in eastern Ukraine.

The President engaged in this course of conduct for the benefit of his presidential reelection, to harm the election prospects of a political rival, and to influence our nation's upcoming presidential election to his advantage. In doing so, the President placed his own personal and political interests above the national interests of the United States, sought to undermine the integrity of the U.S. presidential election process, and endangered U.S. national security.

At the center of this investigation is the memorandum prepared following President Trump's July 25, 2019, phone call with Ukraine's President, which the White House declassified and released under significant public pressure. The call record alone is stark evidence of misconduct; a demonstration of the President's prioritization of his political benefit over the national interest. In response to President Zelensky's appreciation for vital U.S. military assistance, which President Trump froze without explanation, President Trump asked for "a favor though": two specific investigations designed to assist his reelection efforts.<ref name="Intel-Report" />{{Rp|8–9}}</blockquote>

The Republicans of the House Committees had released a countering report the previous day, saying in part that the evidence does not support accusations. "The evidence presented does not prove any of these Democrat allegations, and none of the Democrats' witnesses testified to having evidence of bribery, extortion, or any high crime or misdemeanor," said the draft report.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2019/12/02/house-gop-draft-report-defends-president-trump-impeachment-inquiry/2590245001/ |newspaper=USA Today |first=Bart |last=Jansen |first2=Christal |last2=Hayes |title=House GOP report on impeachment inquiry defends Trump's dealings with Ukraine |date=December 2, 2019 |accessdate=December 12, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.npr.org/2019/12/02/784183484/read-republican-report-on-the-impeachment-inquiry |title=READ: Republican Report On The Impeachment Inquiry |date=December 2, 2019 |accessdate=December 12, 2019}}</ref> This report also painted the push to impeachment as solely politically motivated. Its executive summary states that "The Democrats are trying to impeach a duly elected president based on the accusations and assumptions of unelected bureaucrats who disagreed with President Trump's policy initiatives and processes."<ref>{{cite news |first=Jessica |last=Taylor |url=https://www.npr.org/2019/12/02/784260364/house-gop-rebuts-democrats-impeachment-efforts-no-bribery-extortion-proven |title=House GOP Rebuts Democrats' Impeachment Efforts: No 'Bribery, Extortion' Proven |date=December 2, 2019 |accessdate=December 12, 2019}}</ref>

This report concluded the inquiry stage of the impeachment process and the house then voted on the approved articles of impeachment; [[Impeachment of Donald Trump|Trump was impeached]] on December 18, 2019.

== Responses ==
=== White House ===

In the wake of the inquiry, the White House threatened to shut down all major legislation as political leverage.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.rollcall.com/news/whitehouse/white-house-threatens-to-shut-down-legislative-process-during-impeachment-inquiry |title=White House threatens to shut down legislative process during impeachment inquiry |last=Bennett |first=John T. |date=September 25, 2019|access-date=September 28, 2019 |work=[[Roll Call]]}}</ref> Trump and his surrogates engaged in a misinformation campaign to discredit impeachment,<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2019/09/27/trump-campaign-launches-anti-impeachment-blitz-facebook-repeating-falsehoods-about-four-minority-congresswomen/ |title=Trump campaign launches anti-impeachment blitz on Facebook, targeting four minority congresswomen |work=The Washington Post |first1=Isaac |last1=Stanley-Becker |first2=Tony |last2=Romm |date=September 27, 2019|accessdate=October 4, 2019}}</ref> with Giuliani taking a lead role.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2019/sep/29/rudy-giuliani-donald-trump-ukraine-impeachment-inquiry |title=Giuliani leads battle against intensifying Trump impeachment inquiry |work=The Guardian |first=Ed |last=Pilkington |date=September 30, 2019|access-date=September 30, 2019}}</ref> Efforts focused on attacking Joe Biden and his son<ref name="bbc">{{cite news |title=White House 'tried to cover up details of Trump-Ukraine call' |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-49842895 |work=[[BBC News]] |date=September 26, 2019 |quote=There is no evidence of any wrongdoing by the Bidens. |accessdate=October 1, 2019}}</ref> and attempting to discredit the whistleblower over their motivations and for making the complaint based on [[hearsay]].<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2019/sep/30/donald-trump-has-put-whistleblower-in-danger-lawyers-say-ukraine-impeachment |title=Donald Trump has put whistleblower in danger, lawyers say |first=Ed |last=Pilkington |work=The Guardian |date=September 30, 2019|accessdate=September 30, 2019}}</ref>

On September 30, CNN, citing an analysis by Laura Edelson at [[New York University]]'s [[New York University Tandon School of Engineering|Tandon School of Engineering]], reported that Trump and his reelection campaign had spent hundreds of thousands of dollars on Facebook advertisements to push for his defense. More than 1,800 ads on Trump's Facebook page that mentioned "impeachment" had run the week prior and had been viewed between 16 and 18 million times on Facebook. The analysis indicates the campaign spent between $600,000 and $2&nbsp;million on the ads, which reportedly attempted to rally and enlist people for the "Official Impeachment Defense Task Force". A further $700,000 is believed to have been spent for ads on Pence's Facebook page, which mirrored the content on Trump's.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/09/30/politics/facebook-trump-impeachment/index.html |title=Trump is using Facebook to run thousands of ads about impeachment |last1=O'Sullivan |first1=Donie |last2=Wright |first2=David |date=September 30, 2019 |website=CNN |access-date=October 1, 2019}}</ref>

The White House officially responded to the impeachment proceedings in a letter from White House Counsel Pat Cipollone to House Speaker Pelosi that it would cease all cooperation with the investigation due to a litany of concerns, including that there had been no vote of the full House, and the secrecy of the proceedings. In the October{{nbsp}}8 letter, the White House officially declined to cooperate with what they claimed was an illegitimate effort "to overturn the results of the 2016 election". The eight-page letter said the investigation "violates the Constitution, the rule of law, and every past precedent". Pelosi responded to the letter: "The White House should be warned that continued efforts to hide the truth of the president's abuse of power from the American people will be regarded as further evidence of obstruction."<ref name="bbc Oct 9" /><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.usnews.com/news/politics/articles/2019-10-08/read-white-house-letter-declares-impeachment-inquiry-unconstitutional |title=READ: White House Letter Declares Impeachment Inquiry Unconstitutional |last1=Hagen |first1=Lisa |date=October 8, 2019 |work=US News and World Report |accessdate=October 8, 2019}}</ref><ref name="borger" /><ref name="blake-aaron" /><ref name="NYT Oct 8 2019" />

During an October 17 press conference, White House acting chief of staff Mick Mulvaney said he "was involved with the process" of the freezing of military aid. Mulvaney gave his account of why Trump decided to hold back military aid to Ukraine. One, Trump felt the other European countries were not doing enough. Two, Trump felt Ukraine was a "corrupt place" which included having "corruption related to the DNC server" concerning "what happened in 2016". As a result, reporter [[Jonathan Karl]] told Mulvaney "what you just described is a ''quid pro quo''. It is: 'Funding will not flow unless the investigation into the Democratic server happens as well.'" Mulvaney replied to Karl: "We do that all the time with foreign policy{{nbsp}}... Get over it. There's going to be political influence in foreign policy." Later in the press conference, Mulvaney quoted a third reason on why military aid was frozen: they had yet to cooperate with a U.S. Justice Department investigation into alleged Ukrainian interference in the [[2016 United States presidential election|2016 U.S. presidential election]].<ref name="becket" /><ref name="getoverit">{{cite news |url=https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/donald-trump/mulvaney-acknowledges-trump-held-ukraine-aid-political-reasons-get-over-n1068256 |title=Mulvaney acknowledges Trump held up Ukraine aid for political reasons: 'Get over it' |last=Smith |first=Allan |date=October 17, 2019 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://archive.today/20191024095917/https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/donald-trump/mulvaney-acknowledges-trump-held-ukraine-aid-political-reasons-get-over-n1068256 |archive-date=October 24, 2019 |publisher=[[NBC News]] |accessdate=November 5, 2019}}</ref>

After media reports of these comments circulated, Republicans joined Trump's aides and legal counsel in distancing themselves from his remarks.<ref name="walk back">{{cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/national-security/trumps-envoy-tells-congress-the-president-outsourced-ukraine-policy-to-giuliani/2019/10/17/484b30d0-f0ee-11e9-b648-76bcf86eb67e_story.html |title=After saying Trump held back aid to pressure Ukraine, Mulvaney tries to walk back comments |last=Demirjian |first=Karoun |last2=Hudson |first2=John |date=October 17, 2019 |work=The Washington Post |accessdate=October 18, 2019}}</ref><ref name="Mulvaney walkback">{{cite news |url=https://apnews.com/35cfc12c24494af3a6f0298f4c8fd791 |title=The Latest: Mulvaney says Ukraine remarks were misconstrued |date=October 18, 2019|accessdate=October 20, 2019 |work=Associated Press News}}</ref> Later that same day, Mulvaney issued a statement criticizing the media for their coverage of his comments and denying his earlier remarks, reiterating there was "no ''quid pro quo''" regarding the withheld aid and requests to investigate the Democrats' behavior during the 2016 election.<ref name="Mulvaney walkback" /><ref name="walk back" /><ref name="nyt-quid">{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/10/17/us/politics/mick-mulvaney-trump-ukraine.html |title=Mulvaney Says, Then Denies, That Trump Held Back Ukraine Aid as Quid Pro Quo |last=Shear |first=Michael D. |date=October 17, 2019 |work=The New York Times|access-date=October 20, 2019 |last2=Rogers |first2=Katie |issn=0362-4331}}</ref>

==== Trump ====

{{Tweet|name=Donald Trump|username=realDonaldTrump|date=September 29, 2019|text="...{{nbsp}}If the Democrats are successful in removing the President from office (which they will never be), it will cause a Civil War like fracture in this Nation from which our Country will never heal." Pastor Robert Jeffress, @FoxNews|ID=1178477539653771264|accessdate=October 6, 2019}}
{{Tweet|name=Donald Trump|username=realDonaldTrump|date=October 22, 2019|text=So some day, if a Democrat becomes President and the Republicans win the House, even by a tiny margin, they can impeach the President, without due process or fairness or any legal rights. All Republicans must remember what they are witnessing here—a lynching. But we will WIN!|ID=1186611272231636992}}[[File:Letter from President Trump to House Speaker Nancy Pelosi — December 17, 2019.pdf|thumb|right|Letter from President Trump to House Speaker Nancy Pelosi—December 17, 2019]]

President Trump's first known response was in a phone call with Nancy Pelosi, in which he started out the conversation alluding to background check legislation he knew Pelosi wanted passed.<ref>{{Cite AV media | url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MCpXVhFmxYY | title=Nancy Pelosi on Her Impeachment Phone Call with Trump | publisher=The New Yorker | date=October 14, 2019 | access-date=May 27, 2020}}</ref> Pelosi made no direct allegation that Trump was offering to get the legislation passed in exchange for dropping the investigation, but noted that Trump abruptly changed the subject to his phone call with Ukraine being "perfect." President Trump later took to Twitter, criticizing opponents and praising supporters.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/09/29/trump-twitter-ed-henry-fox-news-010365 |title=Trump launches Twitter tirade against Fox News' Ed Henry |work=Politico |first=David |last=Cohen |date=September 30, 2019|access-date=September 30, 2019}}</ref> He suggested that Representative Schiff, chairman of the House Intelligence Committee, could be arrested for treason,<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/30/us/politics/trump-schiff-treason.html |title=Trump Raises Idea of Arresting House Chairman for Treason |last=Sullivan |first=Eileen |date=September 30, 2019 |work=The New York Times|access-date=September 30, 2019 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> and quoted Pastor [[Robert Jeffress]], who suggested that a "[[Second American Civil War|Civil War-like fracture]]" would occur if Trump were removed from office.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.apnews.com/f7ba2667deda489ea7eb3e173944e734 |title=Trump Warns of Treason, Civil War; GOP Congressman Outraged |last=Kellman |first=Laurie |date=September 30, 2019 |work=Associated Press News|access-date=September 30, 2019}}</ref> Trump described the impeachment inquiry as "a [[Coup d'état|coup]], intending to take away the power of [the] people, their vote, [and] their freedoms",<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/americas/us-politics/trump-impeachment-latest-coup-tweet-democrats-ukraine-call-a9128866.html |title=Trump falsely calls impeachment probe 'a coup' designed to strip citizens of rights in wild Twitter tirade |first1=Jon |last1=Sharman |first2=Andrew |last2=Buncombe |work=The Independent |date=October 2, 2019 |accessdate=October 3, 2019}}</ref> and said the Democrats were "wasting everyone's time and energy on bullshit".<ref>{{Cite news |first=Steve |last=Holland |first2=Jeff |last2=Mason |work=[[Reuters]] |title=Temperamental Trump Blows His Top Over Impeachment Inquiry |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-trump-whistleblower-mood-idUSKBN1WH2O2 |accessdate=October 3, 2019 |date=October 3, 2019}}</ref> He compared the inquiry to [[Lynching in the United States|lynching]] on his Twitter account, saying that "All Republicans must remember what they are witnessing here—a lynching! But we will WIN!"<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/10/22/donald-trump-impeachment-inquiry-lynching-054234 |title=Trump provokes outrage by calling impeachment inquiry 'a lynching' |last=Forgey |first=Quint |date=October 22, 2019 |website=Politico |language=en-US |access-date=October 25, 2019}}</ref>

Trump told supporters at a private event on September 26 that the whistleblower's actions were close to that of a spy, saying, "You know what we used to do in the old days when we were smart? Right? The spies and treason, we used to handle it a little differently than we do now." The remarks were recorded and reported by the ''[[Los Angeles Times]]'' and interpreted as implying execution.<ref name="the Hill retaliation">{{cite web |url=https://thehill.com/homenews/administration/463697-whistleblower-attorney-warns-retaliating-against-client-violates-law |title=Whistleblower attorney warns retaliating against client violates law after Trump comments |last=Wise |first=Justin |date=September 30, 2019 |website=The Hill|access-date=September 30, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Pettypiece |first1=Shannon |title=Trump says those who gave info to the whistleblower are like spies, reports say |url=https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/white-house/trump-says-our-country-stake-whistleblower-account-made-public-n1059011 |accessdate=October 1, 2019 |work=[[NBC News]] |date=September 27, 2019}}</ref> On September 30, Trump said "we're trying to find out" who the whistleblower was.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Jackson |first1=David |title=Donald Trump: 'We're trying to find out' the identity of whistleblower who made Ukraine complaint |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2019/09/30/donald-trump-trying-find-out-who-ukraine-whistleblower/3822241002/ |accessdate=October 1, 2019 |work=[[USA Today]] |date=September 30, 2019}}</ref>

On October 3, Trump told reporters that China should also investigate the Bidens.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Segers |first1=Grace |last2=Watson |first2=Kathryn |last3=Becket |first3=Stefan |title=Trump suggests Ukraine and China should investigate Bidens—live updates |url=https://www.cbsnews.com/live-news/donald-trump-impeachment-inquiry-latest-updates-today-2019-10-03/ |accessdate=October 4, 2019 |work=CBS News |date=October 3, 2019}}</ref> Vice President Pence echoed his support later the same day.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Lejeune |first=Tristan |title=Pence defends Trump's calls for Ukraine to investigate Biden |url=https://thehill.com/homenews/administration/464246-pence-defends-trumps-calls-for-ukraine-to-investigate-biden |accessdate=October 4, 2019 |work=The Hill |date=October 3, 2019}}</ref>

On November 6, [[Donald Trump Jr.]] tweeted a [[Breitbart News]] link purportedly revealing the name of the whistleblower.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/2019/11/06/donald-trumps-son-tweets-alleged-name-whistleblower-triggered/ |title=Donald Trump's son tweets alleged name of whistleblower who triggered impeachment inquiry |last=Riley-Smith |first=Ben |date=November 6, 2019 |work=The Telegraph|access-date=November 6, 2019 |language=en-GB |issn=0307-1235}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/rachelsandler/2019/11/06/donald-trump-jr-slammed-for-outing-alleged-whistleblower-as-major-news-outlets-decline-to-publish-name/|title=Donald Trump Jr. Slammed For Outing Alleged Whistleblower, As Major News Outlets Decline To Publish Name|last=Sandler|first=Rachel|date=November 6, 2019|website=Forbes|language=en-US|access-date=November 8, 2019}}</ref>

As witnesses like Vindman and Yovanovitch gave public testimony, Trump has repeatedly attacked them on Twitter.<ref>{{cite news|title=Attacking witnesses is Trump's core defense strategy in fighting impeachment|last1=Viebeck|first1=Elise|last2=Stanley-Becker|first2=Isaac|date=November 18, 2019|work=The Washington Post|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/attacking-witnesses-is-trumps-core-defense-strategy-in-fighting-impeachment/2019/11/18/6ad8e660-07e1-11ea-8ac0-0810ed197c7e_story.html}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/11/19/republicans-reject-trump-attacks-impeachment-witnesses-071813|title=Republicans reject Trump's attacks on impeachment witnesses|last=Zanona|first=Melanie|date=November 19, 2019|work=Politico|accessdate=November 21, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/18/politics/trump-impeachment-defense-jennifer-williams-gordon-sondland/index.html|title=Trump attacks another witness as his impeachment defense faces new tests|last=Collinson|first=Stephen|date=November 18, 2019|work=CNN|accessdate=November 21, 2019}}</ref> He often describes them as "people I never heard of" and as "[[Never Trumper]]s", suggesting they are motivated only by opposition to his presidency.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/10/29/donald-trump-alexander-vindman-testimony-061018|title=Trump goes on Twitter tear after White House official condemns his Ukraine call|last=Forgey|first=Quint|date=October 29, 2019|work=Politico|accessdate=November 21, 2019}}</ref> He tweeted a criticism of Yovanovitch during her testimony, which Schiff read to her while she was still on the stand; she described the effect of such comments as "very intimidating".<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/15/politics/public-impeachment-hearings-day-2/index.html|title=Former U.S. ambassador to Ukraine tells impeachment inquiry she was 'shocked and devastated' after being removed from her post|last1=Herb|first1=Jeremy|last2=Raju|first2=Manu|date=November 15, 2019|work=CNN|accessdate=November 21, 2019}}</ref> Attacks on Vindman by the White House and Trump allies, who have questioned his patriotism, have caused him to consult with the Army about possible concerns for his safety and that of his family.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/19/politics/vindman-trump-attack-army-safety/index.html|title=Alexander Vindman has reached out to Army about his family's safety amid attacks by Trump and GOP lawmakers|last=Browne|first=Ryan|date=November 19, 2019|work=CNN|accessdate=November 21, 2019}}</ref>

On December 17, Trump sent Speaker Pelosi a six-page letter objecting to the impeachment process and articles. ''The New York Times'', ''The Washington Post'', ''Politifact'', and CNN reported about the many false or misleading claims in the letter.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/12/17/president-trumps-written-tirade-nancy-pelosi-annotated/ |date=December 17, 2019 |title=Analysis: President Trump's written tirade to Nancy Pelosi, annotated|first1=Aaron|last1=Blake |website=Washington Post}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.politifact.com/article/2019/dec/17/fact-check-trumps-letter-pelosi-about-impeachment-/ |title=Fact-checking falsehoods in Trump's letter to Pelosi|website=PolitiFact |first=Jon |last=Greenberg |first2=Louis |last2=Jacobson |first3=Bill |last3=McCarthy |first4=Amy |last4=Sherman |first5=Miriam |last5=Valverde |date=December 17, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/12/17/politics/fact-check-trump-impeachment-letter-to-pelosi/index.html|title=Fact check: Trump's wild letter to Pelosi is filled with false and misleading claims|first=Daniel |last=Dale |first2=Tara |last2=Subramaniam |website=CNN}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2019/12/17/us/politics/trump-pelosi-letter.html |date=December 17, 2019 |title=Read Trump's Letter to Pelosi Protesting Impeachment|first=Linda |last=Qui |website=New York Times}}</ref>

=== Whistleblowers and their lawyers ===

[[Andrew P. Bakaj]], the lead attorney representing the whistleblowers, sent a joint letter to Maguire on September 28, made public on September 29, in which they raised concerns about the language used by Trump, amongst other things.
