In the letter, the lawyers state "The events of the past week have heightened our concerns that our client's identity will be disclosed publicly and that, as a result, our client will be put in harm's way." The letter also mentioned the $50,000 "bounty" that two conservative Trump supporters have offered as a reward for information about the whistleblower.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-49881847 |title=Trump is endangering whistleblower, lawyers warn |date=September 30, 2019 |work=BBC News|access-date=September 30, 2019}}</ref>

[[Mark Zaid]], co-counsel for the whistleblower, said in a statement in September 2019 that whistleblowers' identities are protected by law and cited testimony by Maguire which drew upon the [[Whistleblower Protection Act]]. The statement was released after Trump questioned on Twitter the validity of the whistleblower's statements.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://thehill.com/homenews/administration/463687-trump-white-house-trying-to-find-out-whistleblowers-identity |title=Trump: White House 'trying to find out' whistleblower's identity |last=Lejeune |first=Tristan |date=September 30, 2019 |website=The Hill|access-date=September 30, 2019}}</ref> Bakaj took to Twitter to issue a warning on September 30 that the whistleblower is entitled to anonymity, is protected by laws and policies, and is not to be retaliated against; to do so would violate federal law.<ref name="the Hill retaliation" /> Bakaj argued in an October 25 ''[[Washington Post]]'' op-ed that the identity of his client is no longer pertinent after further events corroborated his client's account of the matter.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/outlook/we-represent-the-whistleblower-their-identity-is-no-longer-relevant/2019/10/25/d2ff25a2-f6a1-11e9-8cf0-4cc99f74d127_story.html |date=October 25, 2019 |title=We represent the whistleblower. Their identity is no longer relevant. |last1=Zaid |first1=Mark S. |last2=Bakaj |first2=Andrew P. |work=The Washington Post|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191030181150/https://www.washingtonpost.com/outlook/we-represent-the-whistleblower-their-identity-is-no-longer-relevant/2019/10/25/d2ff25a2-f6a1-11e9-8cf0-4cc99f74d127_story.html|archive-date=October 30, 2019|access-date=November 5, 2019}}</ref>

On November 7, Bakaj sent a letter to the White House warning Trump to "cease and desist" calling for the public disclosure of the whistleblower's identity and "engaging in rhetoric and activity that places [the whistleblower] and their family in physical danger". The lawyer said the president would be legally and morally liable if anyone were to be "physically harmed as a result of his, or his surrogates', behavior".<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/07/politics/ukraine-whistleblower-trump-cease-and-desist/index.html|title=Lawyer for Ukraine whistleblower sends White House cease and desist letter to stop Trump's attacks|last=LeBlanc|first=Paul|date=November 7, 2019|work=CNN|accessdate=November 11, 2019}}</ref>

=== Politicians ===

[[File:Representative John Lewis Says It's Time to Begin Impeachment Proceedings.webm|thumb|Representative [[John Lewis]] says on September 24, 2019, "The time to begin impeachment proceedings, against this president, has come"]]

A majority of House members voted in favor of initiation of the impeachment inquiry, including 231 Democrats, and one independent,<ref name="autogenerated1" /><ref name="Majority">{{Cite news |url=https://www.politico.com/story/2019/09/25/majority-of-house-supports-impeachment-inquiry-1512897 |title=Majority of House supports impeachment inquiry |last=Cheney |first=Kyle |date=October 3, 2019 |work=[[Politico]] |accessdate=October 6, 2019}}</ref> Justin Amash from Michigan,<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2019/us/politics/trump-impeachment-congress-list.html |title=Complete List: Who Supports an Impeachment Inquiry Against Trump? |last1=Parlapiano |first1=Alicia |date=October 3, 2019 |work=The New York Times |accessdate=October 6, 2019 |last2=Kao |first2=Jason |last3=Cochrane |first3=Emily |last4=Edmondson |first4=Catie}}</ref> who left the Republican Party on July 4, 2019, in the wake of his protests about holding Trump accountable.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/congress/rep-justin-amash-announces-he-s-leaving-republican-party-n1026561 |title=Rep. Justin Amash announces he's leaving Republican Party |last=Burman |first=Max |date=July 4, 2019 |work=[[NBC News]]|access-date=September 25, 2019}}</ref> Amash became a leading supporter of impeachment after the whistleblower report was released, saying the call script was a "devastating indictment of the president".<ref>{{cite web |url=https://thehill.com/homenews/house/462990-amash-trump-call-with-ukrainian-president-is-a-devastating-indictment-of-the |title=Amash: Trump's Ukraine call a 'devastating indictment of the president' |last=Wise |first=Justin |date=September 25, 2019 |website=The Hill |access-date=September 27, 2019}}</ref>

Republicans have largely focused their complaints on the inquiry process, particularly on the use of closed-door hearings, which they allege are secret Democratic hearings closed to Republicans.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://twitter.com/SteveScalise/status/1187045316316536834 |title=Democrats are trying to deny Republican Members of Congress access to Schiff's secret impeachment proceedings. What are they hiding?? Enough is enough! The American people deserve transparency! This Democrat scheme to impeach @realDonaldTrump behind closed doors cannot continue.pic.twitter.com/ernM1x73m9 |last=Scalise |first=Steve |date=October 23, 2019 |website=Twitter |access-date=October 23, 2019}}</ref> Forty-eight Republicans are members of the three committees jointly holding the hearings and thus are entitled to attend the hearings, and dozens have done so.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://theweek.com/speedreads/873958/matt-gaetz-claimed-gop-shut-impeachment-hearing-48-republicans-welcome-room |title=Matt Gaetz claimed the GOP was shut out of an impeachment hearing. 48 Republicans were welcome in the room. |last=Krawczyk |first=Kathryn |date=October 23, 2019 |work=The Week |accessdate=October 25, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |first=Ursula |last=Perano |date=October 23, 2019 |url=https://www.axios.com/house-republicans-scif-impeachment-inquiry-67cf94d5-b2be-4420-ab4c-0582eb1369ef.html |title=13 Republicans involved in impeachment protest already have access to hearings |website=Axios}}</ref> In response to Republican complaints, Chairman Schiff pointed out that past impeachment inquiries began with an investigation by an independent prosecutor appointed by the Justice Department—the Watergate investigators in the case of Richard Nixon and the Whitewater prosecutors regarding Bill Clinton. "Unlike in past impeachment proceedings in which Congress had the benefit of an investigation conducted in secret by an independent prosecutor, we must conduct the initial investigation ourselves," Schiff said. "This is the case because the Department of Justice under Bill Barr expressly declined to investigate this matter after a criminal referral had been made."<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2019/10/25/trump-impeachment-inquiry-why-didnt-doj-look-harder-ukraine-call/4024155002/ |title=As Trump impeachment probe heats up, some say Congress is doing inquiry the Justice Department should've done |last=Johnson |first=Kevin |date=October 25, 2019 |work=USA Today |accessdate=October 25, 2019}}</ref>

==== For impeachment inquiry ====

A notable Republican critic of Trump, Senator [[Mitt Romney]] of [[Utah]], called Trump's actions "troubling in the extreme" and "wrong and appalling". Romney said it strained credulity to say Trump's actions were anything other than politically motivated.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.sltrib.com/news/politics/2019/10/04/mitt-romney-says-it/ |title=Mitt Romney ratchets up his response to Trump accusations going from 'troubling' to 'appalling' |last=Wood |first=Benjamin |date=October 4, 2019 |work=[[The Salt Lake Tribune]]|access-date=October 4, 2019}}</ref> However, in a later interview with ''[[The Salt Lake Tribune]]'', Romney called his relationship with Trump "cordial and cooperative".<ref name="burr" /> He also refrained from indicating publicly whether he thinks the Senate should remove Trump from office, stating "an impeachment process is not a matter of public opinion or public parties. It's a matter of deliberation for the Senate."<ref name="burr">{{cite news |last1=Burr |first1=Thomas |title=Sen. Mitt Romney's sometimes rocky relationship with President Trump is 'cordial' and 'cooperative', Utah senator says |url=https://www.sltrib.com/news/politics/2019/11/25/sen-mitt-romneys/ |accessdate=November 27, 2019 |work=The Salt Lake Tribune |date=November 25, 2019}}</ref>

[[Phil Scott (politician)|Phil Scott]], the [[Governor of Vermont]],<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/26/us/politics/phil-scott-vermont-governor-impeachment.html |title=Phil Scott Is First G.O.P. Governor to Back Impeachment Inquiry |last=Astor |first=Maggie |date=September 26, 2019 |work=The New York Times|access-date=September 27, 2019 |issn=0362-4331}}</ref> became the first Republican governor to support the impeachment inquiry. [[Charlie Baker]], the Republican [[Governor of Massachusetts]], also announced his support.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/09/26/two-republican-governors-say-they-support-impeachment-inquiry-trump/ |title=Two Republican governors say they support impeachment inquiry of Trump |last=Thebault |first=Reis |date=September 26, 2019 |work=The Washington Post|access-date=September 27, 2019 |issn=0190-8286}}</ref> Republican [[Maryland Governor]] [[Larry Hogan]] later announced his support for an inquiry, though clarifying he did not yet support impeachment itself.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/10/11/larry-hogan-trump-impeachment-044378 |title=Larry Hogan comes out in support of Trump impeachment inquiry |last=Marshall |first=Abbey |date=October 11, 2019 |work=[[Politico]]|access-date=October 11, 2019 |issn=0190-8286}}</ref>

On October 18, [[John Kasich]], former [[Governor of Ohio]]  and a CNN political commentator since January 2019, publicly said President Trump should be impeached. Until this point, he had argued that there was not enough evidence to impeach him.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Iyer |first=Kaanita |date=October 18, 2019 |title=Former Republican Ohio Gov. John Kasich says he's now for impeaching Trump |url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/10/18/politics/kasich-calls-for-trump-impeachment/index.html |work=CNN |access-date=October 18, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |last=Klar |first=Rebecca |date=October 18, 2019 |title=Kasich says he'd back impeachment |url=https://thehill.com/homenews/house/466487-kasich-says-hed-back-impeachment |work=The Hill |access-date=October 18, 2019}}; {{Cite news |last1=Stetler |first1=Brian |title=John Kasich signs with CNN as senior political commentator |url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/01/15/media/john-kasich-cnn-contributor/index.html |work=CNN |date=January 15, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |last1=Tani |first1=Maxwell |title=Why Is CNN Paying John Kasich to Seemingly Trial-Balloon a 2020 Run? |url=https://www.thedailybeast.com/why-is-cnn-paying-john-kasich-to-seemingly-trial-balloon-a-2020-run |date=February 19, 2019}}</ref>

During the fourth [[2020 Democratic Party presidential debates and forums|2020 Democratic Party presidential debate]], [[Andrew Yang]] said that while he supports impeaching Trump, he believes it may not be successful and would not solve the issues that led to Trump's election.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/10/15/october-democratic-debate-transcript/|title=The October Democratic debate transcript|date=October 15, 2019|website=Washington Post|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191016035331/https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/10/15/october-democratic-debate-transcript/|archive-date=October 16, 2019|access-date=October 16, 2019}}</ref> He later said "Trump thrives on attention, even negative attention".<ref>{{cite news |last1=LeBlanc |first1=Paul |title=Yang says impeachment may not help the Democrats in 2020 |url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/11/21/politics/andrew-yang-impeachment-2020-cnntv/index.html |accessdate=November 21, 2019 |work=CNN |date=November 21, 2019}}</ref>

==== Against impeachment inquiry ====

Senator [[Lindsey Graham]] (R-South Carolina) criticized the whistleblower, calling the complaint hearsay and a sham.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/10/01/politics/lindsey-graham-defends-trump-whistleblower/index.html |title=How Lindsey Graham's support for Trump—a man he once called a "jackass"—has evolved |last1=Barrett |first1=Ted |date=October 1, 2019 |work=[[CNN]] |accessdate=October 4, 2019}}</ref>

On October 3, 2019, House Republican leader [[Kevin McCarthy (California politician)|Kevin McCarthy]] called on Pelosi to suspend the inquiry and requested answers to 10 questions before it moved forward.<ref>{{cite news |work=[[CNN]] |first=Haley |last=Byrd |url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/10/03/politics/mccarthy-pelosi-suspend-inquiry/index.html |title=Kevin McCarthy calls on Nancy Pelosi to suspend impeachment inquiry |date=October 3, 2019}}</ref> Several Republican politicians, including Representative Jordan and former South Carolina Representative [[Trey Gowdy]], who had been stout defenders of congressional oversight during the Obama Administration and the [[Investigation into the 2012 Benghazi attack]], joined Trump's resistance to the investigation.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/powerpost/gop-players-in-benghazi-probe-drop-strong-defense-of-congressional-oversight/2019/10/09/9dc2a99e-eaa4-11e9-9c6d-436a0df4f31d_story.html |title=GOP players in Benghazi probe drop strong defense of congressional oversight |last1=DeBonis |first1=Mike |date=October 10, 2019 |work=The Washington Post |last2=Bade |first2=Rachael}}</ref>

On October 23, more than two dozen Republican members of the House—led by Representative Gaetz and with Trump's prior knowledge and assent—staged a protest against impeachment proceedings by entering the SCIF where a hearing was about to commence, some carrying cellphones in violation of security protocols.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/10/23/politics/republicans-storm-impeachment-inquiry-deposition-laura-cooper/index.html |title=Impeachment probe deposition under way following Republicans storming hearing room |last1=Raju |first1=Manu |date=October 23, 2019 |work=CNN |last2=Herb |first2=Jeremy}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2019-10-23/poll-finds-highest-support-for-inquiry-yet-impeachment-update |title=Cooper Testimony Starts After GOP Disruption: Impeachment Update |last1=Sully |first1=Evan |date=October 23, 2019 |work=Bloomberg}}</ref> The protest caused a five-hour stand-off during which the [[Sergeant at Arms of the United States House of Representatives|House Sergeant at Arms]] was summoned to intervene.<ref>{{cite news |first=Andrew |last=Desiderio |first2=Melanie |last2=Zanona |date=October 23, 2019 |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/10/23/impeachment-republicans-trump-055688 |title=Impeachment deposition delayed after Republicans storm proceedings |website=Politico}}</ref> Days earlier, Gaetz—who is not a member of any of the three committees—had entered the hearings and was instructed to leave after a parliamentarian ruling.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.cnn.com/politics/live-news/impeachment-inquiry-10-14-2019/h_fe1782530e232ad17a875ad1e3ec8823 |first=Jeremy |last=Herb |first2=Manu |last2=Raju |first3=Laurie |last3=Ure |title=A GOP congressman says he was kicked out of other committees' deposition of Fiona Hill |date=October 14, 2019 |website=CNN}}</ref>

On October 24, Senator Graham, chair of the [[United States Senate Committee on the Judiciary|Senate Judiciary Committee]] proposed a Senate resolution ({{nowrap|[https://www.congress.gov/116/bills/sres378/BILLS-116sres378is.pdf S. Res 378]}}) condemning the closed door impeachment process<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.judiciary.senate.gov/press/rep/releases/chairman-graham-introduces-resolution-condemning-house-of-representatives-closed-door-impeachment-process |title=Chairman Graham Introduces Resolution Condemning House of Representatives' Closed Door Impeachment Process |publisher=Senate Judiciary Committee |date=October 24, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |last=Zhou |first=Li |title='I'm not here to tell you that Donald Trump's done nothing wrong:' Lindsey Graham takes on impeachment process |url=https://www.vox.com/2019/10/24/20930509/lindsey-graham-resolution-condemn-house-impeachment-inquiry |website=Vox |accessdate=October 31, 2019 |date=October 24, 2019}}</ref> and urging the House to hold a formal vote to initiate the impeachment inquiry, which by October 28, 50 Republican senators cosponsored.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.judiciary.senate.gov/press/rep/releases/volume-ii-senate-gop-condemns-house-of-representatives-closed-door-impeachment-process |website=senate.gov |accessdate=December 12, 2019 |title=Volume II: Senate GOP Condemns House of Representatives' Closed Door Impeachment Process |date=October 28, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |last1=Everett |first1=Burgess |last2=Cook |first2=Nancy |title=After McConnell advice, Trump lays off GOP senators on impeachment |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/10/30/trump-senate-republicans-062360 |accessdate=October 31, 2019 |work=Politico |date=October 30, 2019}}</ref> {{as of|2019|11}}, only three Republican Senators, of the 53 in the Senate, [[Susan Collins]] of Maine, [[Lisa Murkowski]] of Alaska, and Mitt Romney of Utah, declined to cosponsor the resolution opposing the impeachment process.<ref>{{cite news |first=Adam |last=Edelman |date=November 9, 2019 |url=https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/trump-impeachment-inquiry/only-3-senate-republicans-aren-t-defending-trump-impeachment-inquiry-n1078906|title=Only 3 Senate Republicans aren't defending Trump from the impeachment inquiry. Here's why.|website=NBC News|access-date=November 10, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://thehill.com/homenews/senate/467842-murkowski-collins-say-they-wont-co-sponsor-grahams-impeachment-resolution|title=Murkowski, Collins say they won't co-sponsor Graham's impeachment resolution|last=Carney|first=Jordain|date=October 28, 2019|website=The Hill|access-date=November 10, 2019}}</ref>

As the articles of impeachment moved to a vote before the full House and referral to the Senate for trial, Senate majority leader Mitch McConnell met with White House Counsel [[Pat Cipollone]] and congressional liaison [[Eric Ueland]], later stating, "everything I do during this I'm coordinating with the White House counsel. There will be no difference between the president's position and our position as to how to handle this."<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://thehill.com/homenews/senate/474399-mcconnell-says-hell-be-in-total-coordination-with-white-house-on-impeachment|title=McConnell says he'll be in 'total coordination' with White House on impeachment trial strategy|first=Jordain|last=Carney|date=December 12, 2019|website=TheHill}}</ref> McConnell also said there was "no chance" the Senate would convict Trump and remove him from office while declaring his wish that all Senate Republicans would acquit Trump of both articles of impeachment.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Egan |first1=Lauren |title=McConnell: 'There's no chance' Trump is removed from office |url=https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/trump-impeachment-inquiry/mcconnell-there-s-no-chance-trump-removed-office-n1101286 |accessdate=December 16, 2019 |date=December 13, 2019}}</ref> Two days later, Judiciary Committee chairman Graham said, "I am trying to give a pretty clear signal I have made up my mind. I'm not trying to pretend to be a fair juror here{{nbsp}}... I will do everything I can to make [the impeachment trial] die quickly."<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/12/14/politics/lindsey-graham-trump-impeachment-trial/index.html |date=December 14, 2019 |title='I'm not trying to pretend to be a fair juror here': Graham predicts Trump impeachment will 'die quickly' in Senate|first=Veronica |last=Stracqualursi|website=CNN}}</ref> The Constitution requires senators to take an impeachment oath, which by Senate rules then in effect stated, "I will do impartial justice according to the Constitution and laws, so help me God."<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://thehill.com/homenews/house/474487-rep-demings-senator-mcconnell-violated-oath-must-recuse-himself|title=House Democrat calls on McConnell to recuse himself from impeachment trial|first=Martin|last=Johnson|date=December 13, 2019|website=TheHill}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.govinfo.gov/content/pkg/CDOC-99sdoc33/html/CDOC-99sdoc33.htm|title=PROCEDURE AND GUIDELINES FOR IMPEACHMENT TRIALS IN THE UNITED STATES SENATE (REVISED EDITION)|website=www.govinfo.gov|access-date=December 15, 2019}}</ref>

House Democrats [[Collin Peterson]] of Minnesota and [[Jeff Van Drew]] of New Jersey, the only two Democrats to vote against the initial October resolution, went public with their intentions to again vote against impeachment ahead of the House vote.<ref name="PetersonAgainst">{{cite news |url=https://www.mprnews.org/story/2019/12/14/collin-peterson-says-likely-vote-against-impeachment |title=Peterson says he'll likely vote against impeachment |website=MPR News |date=December 14, 2019 |author=MPR News Staff}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.politico.com/news/2019/12/15/jeff-van-drew-party-switch-085169 |title=Jeff Van Drew party switch came as Democrats abandoned him |website=Politico |date=December 15, 2019 |last=Friedman |first=Matt}}</ref> Peterson issued that his "biggest problem" was that impeachment was always sought after by Democrats, "[T]hey've spent a year trying to figure out how they can make a case for it. That's backwards. I just don't agree with this."<ref name="PetersonAgainst" />

=== Legal professionals and academics ===
==== Academics ====

Some historians and diplomats have called the severity of the allegations "unprecedented" in American history.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-behavior-with-ukraine-stupid-and-unprecedented-historian-2019-9 |title=Trump's actions with Ukraine were 'profoundly stupid' and beyond anything any president has ever done, historians and veteran diplomats say |last=Haltiwanger |first=John |website=[[Business Insider]]|access-date=September 29, 2019 |date=September 28, 2019}}</ref> Elaine Kamarck of the [[Progressive Policy Institute]] has described how this inquiry is different from Nixon's Watergate: "the president himself is directly involved in all four of the likely articles of impeachment": obstruction of justice, violation of federal election law (a possible constitutional abuse of power), obstruction of Congress, and violation of the emoluments clause.<ref name="Kamarck_10/18/2019">{{cite web|url=https://www.brookings.edu/blog/fixgov/2019/10/18/all-roads-lead-to-putin-this-week-in-impeachment/|title=All roads lead to Putin: This week in impeachment|last=Kamarck|first=Elaine|date=October 18, 2019|publisher=[[Brookings Institution]]|access-date=November 17, 2019}}</ref>

Some academics responded to tweets by Trump in which he quoted [[Robert Jeffress]], a prominent [[Southern Baptist]] pastor who warned of a "Civil War-like fracture" if Democrats continued the inquiry. On Twitter, [[Harvard Law School]] professor John Coates cautioned that the tweet was an independent basis for impeachment as the sitting president was threatening civil war if Congress exercised its constitutionally authorized power.<ref name="civil war quote">{{cite web |url=https://www.newsweek.com/trump-civil-war-tweet-grounds-impeachment-1462044 |title=Trump's 'Civil War' Quote Tweet Is Actually Grounds for Impeachment, Says Harvard Law Professor |last=Hutzler |first=Alexandra |date=September 30, 2019 |website=[[Newsweek]] |access-date=October 1, 2019}}</ref> A fellow faculty member of Harvard Law, [[Laurence Tribe]], agreed but cautioned that, due to the typical tone of Trump's tweets, the statement could be interpreted as "typical Trumpian [[bloviating]]" that would not be taken seriously or literally.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.huffpost.com/entry/john-coates-donald-trump-civil-war-tweet-impeachment_n_5d926a6ae4b0019647ad2dc7 |title=Trump's 'Civil War' Tweet May Be Grounds For Impeachment: Harvard Law Professor |last=Moye |first=David |date=September 30, 2019 |website=[[HuffPost]]|access-date=October 1, 2019}}</ref>

==== Legal professionals ====

A group of 17 former [[Watergate]] special prosecutors published an opinion piece in ''The Washington Post'' in which they said the public record contains ''[[prima facie]]'' evidence that Trump had committed impeachable acts.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/we-investigated-the-watergate-scandal-we-believe-trump-should-be-impeached/2019/10/10/5cf0c2ce-eb72-11e9-9306-47cb0324fd44_story.html|title=We investigated the Watergate scandal. We believe Trump should be impeached.|last1=17 former Watergate special prosecutors|date=October 10, 2019|work=[[The Washington Post]]|accessdate=October 11, 2019}}</ref> [[Ruth Bader Ginsburg|Supreme Justice Ruth Bader Ginsburg]], briefly spoke about the impeachment after she was directly asked about the [[Supreme Court of the United States|Supreme Court]] intervening in the process after Trump had tweeted the suggestion on December 2. Ginsburg highlighted the reactive nature of the U.S. Judicial system, and cautioned that any senator who shows bias before the trial should not be allowed to serve as jurors in the impeachment trial, as any legal professional would be disqualified from a case if they acted similarly.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.foxnews.com/politics/ruth-bader-ginsburg-the-president-is-not-a-lawyer|title=Ruth Bader Ginsburg says Trump 'not a lawyer' after he suggests Supreme Court could halt impeachment|last=Stimson|first=Brie|date=December 18, 2019|website=Fox News|language=en-US|access-date=December 19, 2019}}</ref>

''USA Today''{{'}}s Supreme Court correspondent Richard Wolf published an overview of the opinions of various legal experts, including law professors. The University of Texas's [[Sanford Levinson]] says "nobody really knows" how to define the "[[High crimes and misdemeanors#United States|high crimes and misdemeanors]]" of the Constitution's impeachment clause. According to Georgetown University's [[Randy Barnett]], "The Constitution gets violated all the time. That doesn't make the violation of the Constitution a high crime or misdemeanor." Barnett further states that Trump's accusers "have been alleging impeachable offenses since before [he] took the oath of office". The University of Southern California's [[Orin Kerr]] says, "It's about abusing the office, not about violating a technical provision of a particular clause," and {{nowrap|"[Trump}} is] taking care of himself, not taking care of the country."<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Wolf |first1=Richard |title=Article II of the Constitution: Trump's 'right to do whatever I want?' Or a road map for impeachment? |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2019/10/24/impeachment-donald-trump-constitution-violation-emoluments/4056323002/ |accessdate=October 30, 2019 |work=[[USA Today]] |date=October 24, 2019}}</ref>

Following public impeachment inquiry hearings in the Intelligence and Judiciary House committees, more than 850 legal scholars signed an open letter stating Trump committed "impeachable conduct", asserting "his conduct is precisely the type of threat to our democracy that the Founders feared when they included the remedy of impeachment in the Constitution."<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.dallasobserver.com/news/texas-law-professors-sign-open-letter-calling-for-donald-trumps-impeachment-11810447|title=Texas Law Professors Sign Letter Calling for Trump's Impeachment|first=Silas|last=Allen|date=December 11, 2019|website=Dallas Observer |accessdate=December 12, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://medium.com/@legalscholarsonimpeachment/letter-to-congress-from-legal-scholars-6c18b5b6d116|title=Letter to Congress from Legal Scholars|author=Legal Scholars on Impeachment |date=December 6, 2019|website=Medium |accessdate=December 12, 2019}}</ref> Another open letter signed by more than 1500 historians called for impeachment, stating, "it is our considered judgment that if President Trump's misconduct does not rise to the level of impeachment, then virtually nothing does."<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.dailyprincetonian.com/article/2019/12/15-u-affiliated-historians-sign-letter-supporting-impeachment |first=Linh |last=Nguyen |first2=Zachary |last2=Shevin |first3=Sam |last3=Kagan |date=December 17, 2019 |title=15 U.-affiliated historians sign letter supporting impeachment|website=The Princetonian}}</ref><ref name="medium-16dec2019">{{cite web |author1=Historians on Impeachment |title=HISTORIANS' STATEMENT ON THE IMPEACHMENT OF PRESIDENT TRUMP |url=https://medium.com/@historiansonimpeachment/historians-statement-on-the-impeachment-of-president-trump-6e4ed2277b16 |website=[[Medium (website)|Medium]] |accessdate=December 17, 2019 |date=December 16, 2019}}</ref>

=== Others ===

In December 2019, ''[[Christianity Today]]'' published an editorial ("Trump Should Be Removed from Office") calling for Trump's removal from office, asserting among other criticisms that he "attempted to use his political power to coerce a foreign leader to harass and discredit one of the president's political opponents. That is not only a violation of the Constitution; more importantly, it is profoundly immoral."<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.christianitytoday.com/ct/2019/december-web-only/trump-should-be-removed-from-office.html |date=December 19, 2019 |title=Trump Should Be Removed from Office|first=Mark|last=Galli|author-link = Mark Galli|website=ChristianityToday.com}}</ref>

== Public opinion ==

An analysis of polls showed that support for impeachment among the public grew after the Trump–Ukraine scandal first became public knowledge in September 2019, but through mid-December, Americans remained sharply divided on whether Trump should be removed from office.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://fivethirtyeight.com/features/do-americans-support-impeaching-president-trump/ |title=Do Americans Support Impeaching Trump? |last=Bycoffe |first=Aaron |date=December 17, 2019 |website=FiveThirtyEight|access-date=December 17, 2019}}</ref>

In a [[YouGov]] poll on September 24, 2019, respondents said 55% would support, 26% would oppose, and 19% of respondents were undecided on impeachment if Trump was confirmed to have pressured the Ukrainian government.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://today.yougov.com/topics/politics/articles-reports/2019/09/26/impeachment-trump-support-poll-survey-yougov |title=Most Americans support impeachment if Trump pressured Ukraine |last=Ballard |first=Jamie |date=September 26, 2019 |website=[[YouGov]] |access-date=September 26, 2019}}</ref> A [[Marist Poll]] for [[NPR]] and [[PBS]] around the same time frame claimed that a 50–46 plurality approved of the House's decision to start an impeachment inquiry.<ref name="Marist" /> A poll by ''[[Politico]]'' and [[Morning Consult]], released shortly after Pelosi announced her support for the inquiry, said support for impeachment increased seven percentage points week-over-week.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.politico.com/story/2019/09/26/poll-support-impeachment-trump-1515012 |title=Support for impeachment jumps in new poll |work=[[Politico]] |first=Steven |last=Shepard |date=September 26, 2019 |accessdate=September 26, 2019}}</ref> A ''[[Business Insider]]'' poll on September 27 stated that 45% supported an impeachment inquiry, while 30% opposed.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/2019/09/27/america-backs-impeachment-inquiry-donald-trump-new-polls-suggest/ |title=America backs impeachment inquiry into Donald Trump, new polls suggest |last=Sabur |first=Rozina |date=September 27, 2019 |work=The Telegraph|access-date=September 27, 2019 |issn=0307-1235}}</ref> A September 30 [[Quinnipiac University]] poll stated that 56% of those polled thought members of Congress who support impeaching President Trump are doing so more on the basis of partisan politics than on the basis of the facts.<ref name="Quinnipiac3642">{{cite web |url=https://poll.qu.edu/national/release-detail?ReleaseID=3642 |title=Support For Impeachment Grows Quinnipiac University National Poll Finds; Majority Of Voters Approve Of Impeachment Inquiry |website=Quinnipiac University Poll |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190930202009/https://poll.qu.edu/national/release-detail?ReleaseID=3642|archive-date=September 30, 2019 |date=September 30, 2019|access-date=September 30, 2019}}</ref>

A poll conducted by ''[[The Economist]]'' and YouGov from October 16, 2019, stated that under half of their polled adults supported impeachment, and most of those respondents also support removal from office. Besides, it noted that a significant proportion of Americans (70% of Republicans, 38% of independents, and 13% of Democrats) believe a [[Deep state in the United States|deep state]] is trying to obstruct or unseat President Trump.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://today.yougov.com/topics/politics/articles-reports/2019/10/16/americans-favor-impeachment-want-trump-removed |title=Americans who favor impeachment want President Trump removed, too |work=[[YouGov]] |access-date=October 19, 2019 |first=Kathy |last=Frankovic |date=October 16, 2019}}</ref> An October 17 poll from the Pew Research Center of 3,487 adults found that 54% were in favor of impeachment and 44% opposed.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.people-press.org/2019/10/17/modest-changes-in-views-of-impeachment-proceedings-since-early-september/ |title=Modest Changes in Views of Impeachment Proceedings Since Early September |date=October 17, 2019 |website=Pew Research Center for the People and the Press| access-date=October 17, 2019}}</ref>

A poll conducted on November 11–15, 2019, by NPR, ''[[PBS NewsHour]]'' and Marist Poll of registered American voters showed 45% of respondents favored impeachment and removal from office, while 44% of those polled opposed the idea.<ref name="Marist 11_20">{{cite news |last1=Marist Poll |title=POLITICSNPR/PBS NewsHour/Marist Poll Results & Analysis |url=http://maristpoll.marist.edu/npr-pbs-newshour-marist-poll-results-analysis-9/#sthash.8BfeK8bz.dpbs |accessdate=November 21, 2019 |publisher=Marist Poll |date=November 20, 2019}}</ref> A poll on November 16–17, 2019, by ''[[ABC News]]'' and ''[[Ipsos]]'', stated that 51% of those polled believe Trump was wrong in how he handled the Ukrainian situation and should be impeached. Ipsos also said 21% of polled American adults had made up their minds on impeachment due to the hearings, while the others polled said they had made up their mind prior to the hearings.<ref name="ABC Ipsos Nov 18">{{cite news|url=https://www.ipsos.com/en-us/news-polls/abc-news-impeachment-hearings-Nov-18|title=ABC News/Ipsos Poll: Impact of the First Days of Impeachment Hearings on American Public Opinion|work=Ipsos|date=November 18, 2019|accessdate=November 19, 2019}}</ref><ref name="ipsos">{{cite web |title=A survey of the American general population |url=https://www.ipsos.com/sites/default/files/ct/news/documents/2019-11/topline-abc-ipsos-impeachment-hearings-11182019.pdf |website=Ipsos |publisher=Ipsos KnowledgePanel |accessdate=November 20, 2019}}</ref>
